### Svelte Quickstart Setup

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/svelte

Configuration and installation guide for setting up an AI SDK project with SvelteKit. Includes environment setup, dependency installation, and API key configuration for OpenAI integration.

```APIDOC
## Svelte Quickstart Setup

### Prerequisites
- Node.js 18 or higher
- pnpm package manager
- OpenAI API key

### Installation Steps

#### 1. Create SvelteKit Application
```bash
npx sv create my-ai-app
cd my-ai-app
```

#### 2. Install Dependencies
```bash
pnpm add -D ai @ai-sdk/openai @ai-sdk/svelte zod
```

**Packages:**
- **ai** - Core AI SDK library for text generation and streaming
- **@ai-sdk/openai** - OpenAI provider for AI SDK
- **@ai-sdk/svelte** - Svelte hooks and utilities
- **zod** - TypeScript-first schema validation

#### 3. Configure Environment Variables

Create `.env.local` file in project root:
```bash
touch .env.local
```

Add OpenAI API Key:
```
OPENAI_API_KEY=xxxxxxxxx
```

Replace `xxxxxxxxx` with your actual OpenAI API key from https://openai.com

### Project Structure
```
my-ai-app/
├── src/
│   └── routes/
│       └── api/
│           └── chat/
│               └── +server.ts
├── .env.local
└── svelte.config.js
```

### Notes
- Vite does not automatically load environment variables to `process.env`
- Import environment variables from `$env/static/private` in SvelteKit server routes
- Run dev server to resolve any type errors: `pnpm dev`
```

### Create Basic API Request with Go OpenAI SDK

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/libraries

Shows how to make a simple Responses API request in Go using the OpenAI SDK. The example creates a client with API key configuration, calls the Responses.New method with context and parameters, handles errors, and outputs the response text.

```go
package main

import (
  "context"
  "fmt"
  "github.com/openai/openai-go/v3"
  "github.com/openai/openai-go/v3/option"
)

func main() {
  client := openai.NewClient(
    option.WithAPIKey("My API Key"), // or set OPENAI_API_KEY in your env
  )
  resp, err := client.Responses.New(context.TODO(), openai.ResponseNewParams{
    Model: openai.F("gpt-5-nano"),
    Input: openai.F("Say this is a test"),
  })
  if err != nil {
    panic(err.Error())
  }
  fmt.Println(resp.OutputText)
}
```

### Basic Server Setup with Fastify (CJS)

Source: https://fastify.dev/

Illustrates a basic Fastify server setup using CommonJS modules. It requires the framework, instantiates it, defines a GET route, and starts the server, handling potential errors.

```javascript
const fastify = require('fastify')({ logger: true })

fastify.get('/', function handler (request, reply) {
  reply.send({ hello: 'world' })
})

fastify.listen({ port: 3000 }, (err) => {
  if (err) {
    fastify.log.error(err)
    process.exit(1)
  }
})
```

### Basic Server Setup with Fastify (ESM)

Source: https://fastify.dev/

Demonstrates a basic Fastify server setup using ECMAScript Modules (ESM). It instantiates Fastify, defines a simple GET route, and starts the server, logging any errors.

```javascript
import Fastify from 'fastify'
const fastify = Fastify({ logger: true })

fastify.get('/', async function handler (request, reply) {
  return { hello: 'world' }
})

try {
  await fastify.listen({ port: 3000 })
} catch (err) {
  fastify.log.error(err)
  process.exit(1)
}
```

### Basic API Request - .NET/C#

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/libraries

Create and execute a basic API request using the OpenAI .NET SDK. This example instantiates the OpenAI client with an API key from environment variables, creates a response request, and outputs the assistant response.

```csharp
using System;
using System.Threading.Tasks;
using OpenAI;

class Program
{
  static async Task Main()
  {
    var client = new OpenAIClient(
      Environment.GetEnvironmentVariable("OPENAI_API_KEY")
    );

    var response = await client.Responses.CreateAsync(new ResponseCreateRequest
    {
      Model = "gpt-5-nano",
      Input = "Say 'this is a test.'"
    });

    Console.WriteLine($"[ASSISTANT]: {response.OutputText()}");
  }
}
```

### Basic API Request - Python

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/libraries

Create and execute a basic API request using the OpenAI Python SDK. This example initializes the OpenAI client, sends a request to the Responses API with the gpt-5-nano model, and prints the output text.

```python
from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI()

response = client.responses.create(
  model="gpt-5-nano",
  input="Write a one-sentence bedtime story about a unicorn."
)

print(response.output_text)
```

### Create Basic API Request with Java OpenAI SDK

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/libraries

Demonstrates a simple OpenAI Responses API request using the Java SDK. The example initializes an OpenAIClient using environment configuration, builds request parameters with model and input text, executes the request, and prints the response output.

```java
import com.openai.client.OpenAIClient;
import com.openai.client.okhttp.OpenAIOkHttpClient;
import com.openai.models.responses.Response;
import com.openai.models.responses.ResponseCreateParams;

public class Main {
  public static void main(String[] args) {
    OpenAIClient client = OpenAIOkHttpClient.fromEnv();
    ResponseCreateParams params = ResponseCreateParams.builder()
      .input("Say this is a test")
      .model("gpt-5-nano")
      .build();
    Response response = client.responses().create(params);
    System.out.println(response.outputText());
  }
}
```

```shell
# Install dependencies from package.json

### Marketplace Installation Flow

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/submit-integration

Handles installations initiated from the Vercel Marketplace. After installation, users are redirected to complete setup on the partner's side and then back to Vercel.

```APIDOC
## Marketplace Installation Flow

### Description
This flow handles installations initiated from the Vercel Marketplace. Post-installation, the user is redirected to the partner's page to complete setup, then redirected back to Vercel via the provided next URL.

### Flow Steps
1. User installs integration from Vercel Marketplace
2. User is redirected to partner's setup page with query parameters
3. Partner completes setup and redirects user to provided next URL

### Query Parameters
- **code** (string) - Required - The authorization code received. Example: `jMIukZ1DBCKXHje3X14BCkU0`
- **teamId** (string) - Optional - The ID of the team (only if a team is selected). Example: `team_LLHUOMOoDlqOp8wPE4kFo9pE`
- **configurationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the configuration. Example: `icfg_6uKSUQ359QCbPfECTAY9murE`
- **next** (string) - Required - Encoded URL to redirect to after installation. Example: `https%3A%2F%2Fvercel.com%2F...`
- **source** (string) - Required - Source of installation. Value: `marketplace`

### Usage
After user completes setup on your side, redirect to the `next` parameter URL to close the popup and continue in Vercel.
```

### GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/verify

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Validates a resources transfer request by verifying the target installation and requesting any necessary information for prerequisite setup. The installation ID in the URL is the target installation ID, not the source.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/verify

### Description
Validate Resources Transfer Request - Vercel uses this endpoint to provide a potential target for the transfer and request necessary information for prerequisite setup. Multiple sources may verify the same transfer. Only transfers that haven't been completed can be verified.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/verify`

### Security
System Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the target installation to transfer resources to. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"
- **providerClaimId** (string) - Required - The provider-specific claim ID for the resource transfer

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **newBillingPlan** (object) - Optional - The new billing plan required for the transfer, only required when the current installation's billing plan is not sufficient

#### Response Codes
- 200 - Success
- 403 - Forbidden
- 404 - Not Found
- 409 - Conflict
- 422 - Unprocessable Entity
```

### GET /installations

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Retrieve installation information for marketplace partners. Used to get details about installed integrations and their configurations.

```APIDOC
## GET /installations

### Description
Retrieve installation details for marketplace partner integrations. This endpoint returns information about active installations.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/installations

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Optional - Specific installation ID to retrieve

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **id** (string) - Installation identifier
- **status** (string) - Installation status (active, inactive, etc.)
- **configuration** (object) - Installation configuration details
- **createdAt** (timestamp) - Installation creation timestamp
- **updatedAt** (timestamp) - Last update timestamp
```

### Deploy Button Installation Flow

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/submit-integration

Handles installations using the Vercel deploy button. Users complete setup on the partner's side, then are redirected back to Vercel with project-specific parameters.

```APIDOC
## Deploy Button Installation Flow

### Description
This flow handles installations triggered by the Vercel deploy button. The user completes setup on the partner's side and is redirected back via the provided next URL. If the integration is already installed, the existing configurationId is passed.

### Query Parameters
- **code** (string) - Required - The authorization code received. Example: `jMIukZ1DBCKXHje3X14BCkU0`
- **teamId** (string) - Optional - The ID of the team (only if a team is selected). Example: `team_LLHUOMOoDlqOp8wPE4kFo9pE`
- **configurationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the configuration. Example: `icfg_6uKSUQ359QCbPfECTAY9murE`
- **next** (string) - Required - Encoded URL to redirect to after installation. Example: `https%3A%2F%2Fvercel.com%2F...`
- **currentProjectId** (string) - Required - The ID of the created project. Example: `QmXGTs7mvAMMC7WW5ebrM33qKG32QK3h4vmQMjmY`
- **external-id** (string) - Optional - Partner's reference identifier. Example: `1284210`
- **source** (string) - Required - Source of installation. Value: `deploy-button`

### Important Notes
If the integration is already installed during the deploy button flow, the redirect URL includes the most recent `configurationId`. Store `configurationId` with an access token to retrieve the corresponding token for existing configurations.
```

### Initialize Split SDK and Evaluate Feature Flag Treatment

Source: https://www.split.io/

Initializes the Split SDK with authentication credentials, waits for the SDK_READY event, retrieves a treatment for a feature flag, and logs the result. Handles three possible treatment states: 'on', 'off', or 'CONTROL' (error state). The SDK is properly destroyed after evaluation to flush data.

```JavaScript
(function() {
  var factory = splitio({
    core: {
      authorizationKey: 'YOUR_SDK_KEY',
      key: 'CUSTOMER_ID'
    }
  });
  var client = factory.client();
  client.on(client.Event.SDK_READY, () => {
    console && console.log('Split SDK is ready to evaluate.');
    var treatment = client.getTreatment('FEATURE_FLAG_NAME');
    console && console.log('Treatment is: ' + treatment);
    if (treatment === 'on') {
      console.log("I'm ON");
    } else if (treatment === 'off') {
      console.log("I'm OFF");
    } else {
      console.log("CONTROL was returned, there was an error");
    }
    client.destroy().then(function() {
      console && console.log('Split SDK data was successfully flushed.');
    });
  });
})();
```

### Start Local Proxy Without Turborepo

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/microfrontends/local-development

This example shows how to start the local microfrontends proxy directly using the command line without relying on Turborepo. The `proxy` script in `package.json` invokes the `microfrontends proxy` command, specifying the configuration file and the local applications to be proxied. This method is an alternative for projects not using Turborepo.

```json
{
  "name": "web",
  "scripts": {
    "dev": "next --port $(microfrontends port)",
    "proxy": "microfrontends proxy microfrontends.json --local-apps web"
  },
  "dependencies": {
    "@vercel/microfrontends": "latest"
  }
}
```

### HTTP Server Setup

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Demonstrates how to set up a basic HTTP server using Go's net/http package. Shows the fundamental pattern for listening and serving requests with automatic HTTP/2 support in Go 1.6+.

```APIDOC
## Server Setup

### Description
Initialize and start an HTTP server with the net/http package.

### Method
GET, POST, and other HTTP methods

### Endpoint
Configurable via ListenAndServe or ListenAndServeTLS

### Functions

#### ListenAndServe
- **addr** (string) - Required - The address and port to listen on (e.g., ":8080")
- **handler** (Handler) - Required - The HTTP handler for processing requests
- **Returns** (error) - Error if the server fails to start

#### ListenAndServeTLS
- **addr** (string) - Required - The address and port to listen on
- **certFile** (string) - Required - Path to the SSL certificate file
- **keyFile** (string) - Required - Path to the SSL key file
- **handler** (Handler) - Required - The HTTP handler for processing requests
- **Returns** (error) - Error if the server fails to start

### Request Example
```go
package main

import (
    "net/http"
    "log"
)

func main() {
    log.Fatal(http.ListenAndServe(":8080", nil))
}
```

### Response
Server listens on specified address and processes incoming HTTP requests according to registered handlers.
```

### ServeMux Pattern Matching Examples in Go

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Provides example patterns for Go ServeMux pattern matching demonstrating method, host, and path matching with wildcards. Includes examples of literal path matching, method-specific patterns, host-based routing, and wildcard segments for dynamic path parameters.

```go
// Pattern examples:
// "/index.html" - matches the path for any host and method
// "GET /static/" - matches GET requests with path beginning with "/static/"
// "example.com/" - matches any request to host "example.com"
// "example.com/{$}" - matches requests to "example.com" with path "/"
// "/b/{bucket}/o/{objectname...}" - matches paths with segments matching pattern
```

### HTTP Server - Basic Server

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Details on how to start a basic HTTP server using `ListenAndServe`, and how to register handlers with `DefaultServeMux` using `Handle` and `HandleFunc`.

```APIDOC
## HTTP Server - Basic Server

### Description
Start an HTTP server to listen for incoming requests. Use `DefaultServeMux` to route requests to specific handlers based on URL patterns.

### Method
ListenAndServe, Handle, HandleFunc

### Endpoints
- `http.ListenAndServe(addr, handler)`
- `http.Handle(pattern, handler)`
- `http.HandleFunc(pattern, handlerFunc)`

### Parameters
#### `ListenAndServe`
- **addr** (string) - Required - The TCP address to listen on (e.g., ":8080").
- **handler** (http.Handler) - Optional - The handler to invoke for requests. If nil, `http.DefaultServeMux` is used.

### Request Example (Basic Server Setup)
```go
package main

import (
	"fmt"
	"log"
	"net/http"
	"html"
)

func main() {
	http.HandleFunc("/bar", func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
		fmt.Fprintf(w, "Hello, %q", html.EscapeString(r.URL.Path))
	})

	http.Handle("/foo", http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
		fmt.Fprintln(w, "This is the /foo handler")
	}))

	log.Println("Starting server on :8080")
	err := http.ListenAndServe(":8080", nil) // nil uses DefaultServeMux
	if err != nil {
		log.Fatalf("Server failed: %v", err)
	}
}
```

### Response Example (for `/bar?name=World`)
```html
"/bar"
```

### Error Handling
- `ListenAndServe` blocks until the server is stopped or an error occurs.
- Errors from `ListenAndServe` typically indicate issues with network binding or configuration.
```

--------------------------------

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-flows

Provision a new resource for an installation. This endpoint initiates asynchronous provisioning of a resource on the provider platform using data collected from user input fields. The provider should start provisioning and return resource credentials before completion.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

### Description
Provision a new resource for the installation. Initiates asynchronous provisioning on the provider platform and returns provisioning response with resource details.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - Installation identifier

#### Request Body
- **resourceName** (string) - Required - Name of the resource
- **billingPlan** (string) - Optional - Billing plan for the resource
- **metadata** (object) - Optional - User-provided configuration data
- **storagePath** (string) - Optional - Storage provider and path

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **resourceId** (string) - Unique resource identifier
- **status** (string) - Resource provisioning status
- **credentials** (object) - Resource access credentials
- **metadata** (object) - Resource metadata

#### Response Example
{
  "resourceId": "resource_123",
  "status": "provisioning",
  "credentials": {"apiKey": "key_value"},
  "metadata": {"created": "2024-01-01"}
}
```

--------------------------------

### GET /v1/installations/{installationId}

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Retrieve a specific installation by ID. Returns the installation's billing plan and notification details using System Authentication.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}

### Description
Get an installation by ID. Retrieve the installation's billing plan and active notifications.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}`

### Security
System Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the installation. If not set, the installation is billed on resource level.
- **notification** (object or null) - Installation's active notification. Example: { "level": "warn", "title": "Account is exceeding the maximum allowed storage on the current plan" }

#### Response Example
{
  "billingPlan": {
    "planName": "premium"
  },
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Account is exceeding the maximum allowed storage on the current plan"
  }
}

#### Error Responses
- **403** - Forbidden
```

### External Installation Flow

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/submit-integration

Handles installations initiated from the partner's application. Uses a specific Vercel URL pattern with query parameters for secure integration setup.

```APIDOC
## External Installation Flow

### Description
This flow handles installations initiated from the partner's application. The partner initiates the process using a Vercel URL and receives parameters to manage the installation.

### Starting Point
`https://vercel.com/integrations/:slug/new`

### Parameters
- **:slug** (string) - Required - The integration name added in the Create Integration form

### Query Parameters
- **code** (string) - Required - The authorization code received. Example: `jMIukZ1DBCKXHje3X14BCkU0`
- **teamId** (string) - Optional - The ID of the team (only if a team is selected). Example: `team_LLHUOMOoDlqOp8wPE4kFo9pE`
- **configurationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the configuration. Example: `icfg_6uKSUQ359QCbPfECTAY9murE`
- **next** (string) - Required - Encoded URL to redirect to after installation. Example: `https%3A%2F%2Fvercel.com%2F...`
- **state** (string) - Required - Random string for CSRF protection, passed back upon completion. Example: `xyzABC123`
- **source** (string) - Required - Source of installation. Value: `external`

### Usage
Initiate the installation from your application by directing users to the above URL with appropriate query parameters.
```

--------------------------------

### Initialize Vercel Code Owners CLI

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/code-owners/getting-started

This command initializes Vercel Code Owners in your repository, optionally migrating an existing CODEOWNERS file. It requires the Vercel CLI to be installed and authenticated. The CLI is executed using package managers like pnpm, yarn, or npm.

```shell
pnpm --package=@vercel-private/code-owners dlx vercel-code-owners init
```

```shell
yarn dlx --package=@vercel-private/code-owners vercel-code-owners init
# For Yarn v1, use: npx --package=@vercel-private/code-owners vercel-code-owners init
```

```shell
npm dlx --package=@vercel-private/code-owners vercel-code-owners init
```

### GET /installations/{integrationConfigurationId}/resources

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Retrieves all resources for a given installation ID. Returns a list of resources associated with the integration installation.

```APIDOC
## GET /installations/{integrationConfigurationId}/resources

### Description
Get all resources for a given installation ID.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://api.vercel.com/v1/installations/{integrationConfigurationId}/resources

### Security
Use bearer token to secure this endpoint.

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **integrationConfigurationId** (string) - Required - The integration configuration ID

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **resources** (array) - Required - Array of resources

#### Error Responses
- **400** - Bad Request
- **401** - Unauthorized
- **403** - Forbidden
- **404** - Not Found
```

### PUT /v1/installations/{installationId}

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-flows

Upsert an installation and requesting user. This endpoint is called during the initial installation setup to create or update an installation record and associate it with a user. Returns a 201 response on successful creation or update.

```APIDOC
## PUT /v1/installations/{installationId}

### Description
Upsert installation and requesting user. Creates or updates an installation record for a product integration and associates it with the requesting user.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/v1/installations/{installationId}

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - Unique identifier for the installation

#### Request Body
- **userId** (string) - Required - ID of the requesting user
- **billingPlan** (string) - Optional - Default billing plan (default: "free")
- **metadata** (object) - Optional - Additional installation metadata

### Response
#### Success Response (201)
- **installationId** (string) - The installation identifier
- **userId** (string) - The requesting user identifier
- **status** (string) - Installation status
- **billingPlan** (string) - Assigned billing plan
```

### Synchronous Agent Execution with Pydantic AI

Source: https://ai.pydantic.dev/

This example demonstrates how to run a Pydantic AI agent synchronously. It configures an agent with static instructions and executes it with a user prompt, returning the LLM's output. This setup requires the 'pydantic_ai' package to be installed.

```python
from pydantic_ai import Agent

# Assuming agent is already configured
# agent = Agent(...)

# Example usage:
# result = agent.run_sync('Where does "hello world" come from?')
# print(result.output)

# The first known use of "hello, world" was in a 1974 textbook about the C programming language.

# 1. We configure the agent to use Anthropic's Claude Sonnet 4.0 model, but you can also set the model when running the agent.
# 2. Register static instructions using a keyword argument to the agent.
# 3. Run the agent synchronously, starting a conversation with the LLM.
# (This example is complete, it can be run "as is", assuming you've installed the `pydantic_ai` package)
# The exchange will be very short: Pydantic AI will send the instructions and the user prompt to the LLM, and the model will return a text response.
# Not very interesting yet, but we can easily add tools, dynamic instructions, and structured outputs to build more powerful agents.
```

### Run Next.js Dev Server in Vercel Sandbox (TypeScript)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/vercel-sandbox

This TypeScript script uses the Vercel Sandbox to clone a Next.js example repository, install its npm dependencies, and start the development server. It then opens the application in a browser and streams logs to the console. The sandbox is configured with a 10-minute timeout and exposes port 3000.

```typescript
import ms from 'ms';
import { Sandbox } from '@vercel/sandbox';
import { setTimeout } from 'timers/promises';
import { spawn } from 'child_process';

async function main() {
  const sandbox = await Sandbox.create({
    source: {
      url: 'https://github.com/vercel/sandbox-example-next.git',
      type: 'git',
    },
    resources: {
      vcpus: 4
    },
    // Timeout in milliseconds: ms('10m') = 600000
    // Defaults to 5 minutes. The maximum is 5 hours for Pro/Enterprise, and 45 minutes for Hobby.
    timeout: ms('10m'),
    ports: [3000],
    runtime: 'node22',
  });

  console.log(`Installing dependencies...`);
  const install = await sandbox.runCommand({
    cmd: 'npm',
    args: ['install', '--loglevel', 'info'],
    stderr: process.stderr,
    stdout: process.stdout,
  });

  if (install.exitCode != 0) {
    console.log('installing packages failed');
    process.exit(1);
  }

  console.log(`Starting the development server...`);
  await sandbox.runCommand({
    cmd: 'npm',
    args: ['run', 'dev'],
    stderr: process.stderr,
    stdout: process.stdout,
    detached: true,
  });

  await setTimeout(500);
  spawn('open', [sandbox.domain(3000)]);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

{
  "version": 3,
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/redirect",
      "status": 308,
      "headers": {
        "Location": "https://example.com/"
      }
    },
    {
      "src": "/blog",
      "dest": "/blog.$wildcard.html"
    }
  ],
  "images": {

    "qualities": [25, 50, 75],
    "localPatterns": [{
      "pathname": "^/assets/.*$",
      "search": ""

      {
        "protocol": "https",
        "hostname": "^via\\.placeholder\\.com$",
        "port": "",
        "pathname": "^/1280x640/.*$",
        "search": "?v=1"
      }
    ]
  },
  "wildcard": [
    {
      "domain": "example.com",
      "value": "en-US"
    },
    {
      "domain": "example.nl",
      "value": "nl-NL"
    },
    {
      "domain": "example.fr",
      "value": "fr"
    }
  ],
  "overrides": {
    "blog.html": {
      "path": "blog"
    }
  },
  "cache": [".cache/**", "node_modules/**"],
  "framework": {
    "version": "1.2.3"
  },
  "crons": [
    {
      "path": "/api/cron",
      "schedule": "* * * * *"
    }
  ]
}
```

### Fastify HTTP Server with TypeScript

Source: https://fastify.dev/

Sets up a basic Fastify HTTP server using TypeScript. It defines a GET route '/ping' with a response schema and starts the server listening on port 3000. This example showcases Fastify's TypeScript integration for type safety.

```typescript
import Fastify, { FastifyInstance, RouteShorthandOptions } from 'fastify'
import { Server, IncomingMessage, ServerResponse } from 'http'

const server: FastifyInstance = Fastify({})

const opts: RouteShorthandOptions = {
  schema: {
    response: {
      200: {
        type: 'object',
        properties: {
          pong: { type: 'string' }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

server.get('/ping', opts, async (request, reply) => {
  return { pong: 'it worked!' }
})

const start = async () => {
  try {
    await server.listen({ port: 3000 })
    const address = server.server.address()
    const port = typeof address === 'string' ? address : address?.port
  } catch (err) {
    server.log.error(err)
    process.exit(1)
  }
}

start()
```

--------------------------------

### Add Second Tool for Temperature Conversion (TypeScript)

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nodejs

This snippet extends the previous example by adding a second tool, `convertFahrenheitToCelsius`, to the LLM's available tools. This allows for more complex interactions where the model can use multiple tools sequentially. All necessary imports and configurations from the previous example are included.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');
    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return { location, temperature };
          },
        }),
        convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
          description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            temperature: z
              .number()
              .describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
            const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
            return { celsius };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    // The rest of the streaming logic would follow here...
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');
    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Pydantic AI Hello World Example (Python)

Source: https://ai.pydantic.dev/

A minimal 'Hello World' example demonstrating how to initialize and run a Pydantic AI agent. It shows setting up the agent with a specific model (Anthropic's Claude Sonnet 4.0) and providing instructions. The example then runs the agent synchronously and prints the output.

```python
from pydantic_ai import Agent

agent = Agent(
    'gateway/anthropic:claude-sonnet-4-0',
    instructions='Be concise, reply with one sentence.',
)

result = agent.run_sync('Where does "hello world" come from?')
print(result.output)
```

### Fastify Route Definition with Schema Validation (JavaScript)

Source: https://fastify.dev/

Defines a Fastify route with a GET method, specifying a request querystring schema and a response schema. It also includes a pre-handler for request validation and a handler to send a response. This example demonstrates basic route setup and validation in Fastify.

```javascript
fastify.route({
  method: 'GET',
  url: '/example',
  schema: {
    querystring: {
      type: 'object',
      properties: {
        name: { type: 'string' }
      },
      required: ['name']
    },
    response: {
      200: {
        type: 'object',
        properties: {
          hello: { type: 'string' }
        }
      }
    }
  },
  preHandler: (request, reply, done) => {
    // E.g. check authentication
    done()
  },
  handler: (request, reply) => {
    reply.send({ hello: 'world' })
  }
})

fastify.listen({ port: 3000 }, (err) => {
  if (err) {
    fastify.log.error(err)
    process.exit(1)
  }
})
```

### Install ngrok on Linux via Apt Package Manager

Source: https://ngrok.com/download

Installs ngrok on Linux systems using the Apt package manager by adding the ngrok repository, updating package lists, and installing the ngrok package. Requires sudo privileges and internet connectivity. This method ensures automatic updates through the system package manager.

```bash
curl -sSL https://ngrok-agent.s3.amazonaws.com/ngrok.asc \
| sudo tee /etc/apt/trusted.gpg.d/ngrok.asc >/dev/null \
&& echo "deb https://ngrok-agent.s3.amazonaws.com bookworm main" \
| sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/ngrok.list \
&& sudo apt update \
&& sudo apt install ngrok
```

### Shopify Storefront API Client Initialization and Query (Ruby)

Source: https://shopify.dev/docs/api/storefront

Provides a Ruby example for initializing the Shopify Storefront API client and performing a product query. It demonstrates how to instantiate the client with shop details and an access token, and then execute a GraphQL query.

```ruby
# Load the access token as per instructions above
store_front_access_token = ''
# Shop from which we're fetching data
shop = 'my-shop.myshopify.com'

# The Storefront client takes in the shop url and the Storefront Access Token for that shop.
storefront_client = ShopifyAPI::Clients::Graphql::Storefront.new( shop, store_front_access_token )

# Call query and pass your query as `data`
my_query = <<~QUERY
  {
    products (first: 3) {
      edges {
        node {
          id
          title
        }
      }
    }
  }
QUERY

products = storefront_client.query(query: my_query)
```

--------------------------------

### Webhook: deployment.integration.action.start

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/deployment-integration-action

Webhook event triggered when a deployment starts an action. Contains installation, action, resource, and deployment identifiers needed to process the action.

```APIDOC
## Webhook: deployment.integration.action.start

### Description
This webhook is triggered when a deployment initiates an integration action. The payload contains all necessary identifiers to retrieve deployment details and process the action.

### Event Type
```
deployment.integration.action.start
```

### Webhook Payload

#### Fields
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The integration installation identifier
- **action** (string) - Required - The action slug name
- **resourceId** (string) - Required - The resource identifier
- **deployment** (object) - Required - Deployment information
  - **id** (string) - The deployment ID

### Payload Example
```json
{
  "installationId": "icfg_1234567",
  "action": "branch",
  "resourceId": "abc-def-1334",
  "deployment": {
    "id": "dpl_568301234"
  }
}
```

### Processing Steps
1. Extract deployment ID from the payload
2. Call GET /v13/deployments/{deploymentId} to retrieve full deployment details
3. Process the action based on action type and resource
4. Update action status using PATCH endpoint with outcomes
5. Return appropriate response to webhook

### Related Endpoints
- GET /v13/deployments/{deploymentId} - Retrieve deployment details
- PATCH /v1/deployments/{deploymentId}/integrations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}/actions/{action} - Update action status

### Notes
- This webhook requires an active integration configuration in the Integration Console
- Ensure webhook handler returns 2xx status code within timeout period
- All provided IDs are required for subsequent API calls
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Create or update an installation with billing plan and notification settings. This endpoint uses User Authentication to ensure proper access control.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}

### Description
Create or update an installation. Configure billing plans and notifications for the installation.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}`

### Security
User Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

#### Request Body
- **billingPlan** (object) - Optional - The billing plan for the installation. If not set, the installation is billed on resource level.
- **notification** (object or null) - Optional - Installation's active notification. Return `null` to remove any current installation notification.

### Request Example
{
  "billingPlan": {
    "planName": "premium"
  },
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Account is exceeding the maximum allowed storage on the current plan"
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200/204)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the installation
- **notification** (object or null) - Installation's active notification

#### Response Example
{
  "billingPlan": {
    "planName": "premium"
  },
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Account is exceeding the maximum allowed storage on the current plan"
  }
}

#### Error Responses
- **400** - Bad Request
- **403** - Forbidden
- **409** - Conflict
```

It involves installing the CLI globally, linking to a Vercel project, building the project, and deploying the pre-built output. This is useful for CI/CD pipelines where source code access is restricted or a trunk-based development workflow is used.

```bash

2 vercel pull --yes --environment=preview --token=YOUR_VERCEL_TOKEN
3 vercel build --token=YOUR_VERCEL_TOKEN
4 vercel deploy --prebuilt --token=YOUR_VERCEL_TOKEN
```

### Runtime Storage Configuration with Plugins

Source: https://nitro.unjs.io/guide/storage

Explains how to dynamically add storage mount points at runtime using Nitro plugins. This example demonstrates mounting a Redis driver using runtime configuration for credentials.

```typescript
import redisDriver from 'unstorage/drivers/redis'

export default defineNitroPlugin(() => {
  const storage = useStorage()
  const driver = redisDriver({
    host: useRuntimeConfig().redis.host,
    port: useRuntimeConfig().redis.port,
    /* other redis connector options */
  })
  storage.mount('redis', driver)
})
```

```typescript
export default defineNitroConfig({
  runtimeConfig: {
    redis: {
      host: '',
      port: 0,
      /* other redis connector options */
    }
  }
})
```

```typescript
export default defineNuxtConfig({
  runtimeConfig: {
    redis: {
      host: '',
      port: 0,
      /* other redis connector options */
    }
  }
})
```

### Install and Configure MDX Rollup Plugin

Source: https://remix.run/docs/en/main/future/vite

To use MDX files in your Remix project with Vite, install the official MDX Rollup plugin and configure it in your Vite setup. The MDX plugin should be placed before the Remix plugin to ensure proper transpilation.

```bash
npm install -D @mdx-js/rollup
```

```javascript
import mdx from "@mdx-js/rollup";
import { vitePlugin as remix } from "@remix-run/dev";
import { defineConfig } from "vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    mdx(),
    remix()
  ],
});
```

--------------------------------

### Install Node Polyfills in Vite Config

Source: https://remix.run/docs/en/main/future/vite

Configure your Vite setup to install global Node polyfills by calling installGlobals() at the top of your Vite config file. This is necessary if your application relied on global Node polyfills provided by the previous server.

```javascript
import { vitePlugin as remix } from "@remix-run/dev";
import { installGlobals } from "@remix-run/node";
import { defineConfig } from "vite";

installGlobals();

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [remix()],
});
```

### Advanced MCP Client Configurations

Source: https://github.com/modelcontextprotocol/servers

Illustrates various MCP client configurations for different servers like filesystem, git, github, and postgres. It shows how to pass arguments, specify commands, and set environment variables.

```json
{
  "mcpServers": {
    "filesystem": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem", "/path/to/allowed/files"]
    },
    "git": {
      "command": "uvx",
      "args": ["mcp-server-git", "--repository", "path/to/git/repo"]
    },
    "github": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-github"],
      "env": {
        "GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN": ""
      }
    },
    "postgres": {
      "command": "npx",
      "args": ["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-postgres", "postgresql://localhost/mydb"]
    }
  }
}
```

### Installation Configuration Webhook

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/submit-integration

Endpoint for receiving installation configuration data from Vercel. Partners should implement this webhook to handle installation events and store configuration details.

```APIDOC
## POST Installation Configuration Webhook

### Description
Partners must implement this webhook endpoint to receive installation configuration data from Vercel. This is where Vercel sends the authorization code and installation details.

### Endpoint
`https://foo.bar.com/vercel-integration-server/v1/installations`

### Method
POST

### Request Body
- **code** (string) - Required - Authorization code for the installation
- **teamId** (string) - Optional - Team ID if installation is scoped to a team
- **configurationId** (string) - Required - Configuration identifier for tracking

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **success** (boolean) - Indicates successful webhook processing
- **configurationId** (string) - Confirmed configuration ID

### Response Example
{
  "success": true,
  "configurationId": "icfg_6uKSUQ359QCbPfECTAY9murE"
}

### Notes
Implement this endpoint to store the configuration and access token for future API calls to Vercel.
```

### Configure Cron Jobs in vercel.json

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/cron-jobs/quickstart

This configuration snippet shows how to define cron jobs within your `vercel.json` file. It specifies the path to be triggered and the schedule using a cron expression. The example schedules a job to run the `/api/hello` path every day at 5:00 AM UTC. The `crons` property accepts an array of job objects, each with a `path` and `schedule`.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://openapi.vercel.sh/vercel.json",
  "crons": [
    {
      "path": "/api/hello",
      "schedule": "0 5 * * *"
    }
  ]
}
```

## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}

### Get Resource

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Retrieves details of a specific resource associated with an installation. This endpoint is secured using System Authentication.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}

### Description
Get a Resource

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"
- **resourceId** (string) - Required - Partner-provided resource ID

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the resource. If not set, the resource is billed on installation level.
  - **id** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID of the resource
  - **metadata** (object) - Required - User-inputted metadata based on the registered metadata schema.
  - **name** (string) - Required - User-inputted name for the resource.
  - **notification** (object) - Resource's active notification. Example: { "level": "warn", "title": "Database is nearing maximum planned size" }
    - **productId** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product. Example: "redis"
    - **protocolSettings** (object)
    - **status** (string) - Required - One of: `ready` | `pending` | `onboarding` | `suspended` | `resumed` | `uninstalled` | `error`
```

### GitHub Actions Workflow for Bun

Source: https://bun.sh/docs/cli/install

This YAML configuration sets up a GitHub Actions workflow to build a project using Bun. It checks out the repository, installs Bun, installs project dependencies using 'bun install', and then builds the application.

```yaml
name: bun-types
jobs:
  build:
    name: build-app
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
    - name: Checkout repo
      uses: actions/checkout@v4
    - name: Install bun
      uses: oven-sh/setup-bun@v2
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: bun install
    - name: Build app
      run: bun run build
```

### Set up React Query Client and Provider

Source: https://vercel.com/templates/starter/tanstack-start-on-vercel

Creates a QueryClient instance and a QueryClientProvider to make React Query available throughout your application. This setup is typically done in your main application file (e.g., main.tsx).

```typescript
import { QueryClient, QueryClientProvider } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import ReactDOM from "react-dom/client";

const queryClient = new QueryClient();
const rootElement = document.getElementById("root") as HTMLElement;

if (!rootElement.innerHTML) {
  const root = ReactDOM.createRoot(rootElement);
  root.render(
    <>
      <QueryClientProvider client={queryClient}>
        {/* Your App components */}
      </QueryClientProvider>
    </>
  );
}
```

### Astro Image Service Configuration Example

Source: https://docs.astro.build/en/reference/image-service-reference

Demonstrates how to configure a custom image service entrypoint and its specific configuration within `astro.config.mjs`. This setup is essential for defining how Astro handles image transformations.

```javascript
import { defineConfig } from "astro/config";

export default defineConfig({
  image: {
    service: {
      entrypoint: "your-entrypoint", // 'astro/assets/services/sharp' | string
      config: {
        // ... service-specific config. Optional.
      }
    }
  },
});
```

### Deploy Puppeteer with Next.js for Web Page Screenshots on Vercel

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/integrating-next-js-and-contentful-for-your-headless-cms

This guide demonstrates setting up Puppeteer with Next.js on Vercel for headless browser automation. It provides a practical example for efficiently generating web page screenshots.

```javascript
import puppeteer from 'puppeteer';

export default async (req, res) => {
  const browser = await puppeteer.launch({
    args: ['--no-sandbox', '--disable-setuid-sandbox']
  });
  const page = await browser.newPage();
  await page.goto('https://example.com');
  const screenshot = await page.screenshot();
  await browser.close();

  res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'image/png');
  res.end(screenshot);
};
```

### GitHub Actions Workflow with Bun CI for Reproducible Builds

Source: https://bun.sh/docs/cli/install

This GitHub Actions workflow demonstrates the use of 'bun ci' for installing dependencies, ensuring reproducible builds. It checks out the code, installs Bun, runs 'bun ci' to install dependencies based strictly on the lockfile, and then builds the application.

```yaml
name: bun-types
jobs:
  build:
    name: build-app
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
    - name: Checkout repo
      uses: actions/checkout@v4
    - name: Install bun
      uses: oven-sh/setup-bun@v2
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: bun ci
    - name: Build app
      run: bun run build
```

### Domain Price Check - TypeScript Example

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/rest-api/reference/endpoints/domains/check-the-price-for-a-domain-deprecated

TypeScript code example demonstrating how to check domain pricing using the Vercel SDK. Shows proper authentication setup and parameter passing for domain price queries.

```APIDOC
## TypeScript Implementation Example

### Description
Example implementation using the Vercel SDK to check domain pricing. Demonstrates authentication, parameter configuration, and result handling.

### Code
```typescript
import { Vercel } from "@vercel/sdk";

const vercel = new Vercel({
  bearerToken: ""
});

async function run() {
  const result = await vercel.domains.checkDomainPrice({
    name: "example.com",
    type: "new",
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug"
  });
  console.log(result);
}

run();
```

### Parameters Explained
- **name** - The domain name to check pricing for (e.g., "example.com")
- **type** - The domain operation type: "new" for new domains, "renewal" for renewals, "transfer" for domain transfers, "redemption" for redemption purchases
- **teamId** - Optional team identifier for team-based operations
- **slug** - Optional team slug as alternative team identifier

### Expected Output
```json
{
  "price": 20,
  "period": 1
}
```
```

### POST /responses (Structured Outputs - Chain of Thought Example - Node.js)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs

Example demonstrating how to use Structured Outputs with `gpt-4o-2024-08-06` to guide a math tutoring session, outputting a step-by-step reasoning process and a final answer adhering to a Zod schema.

```APIDOC
## POST /responses (Chain of Thought - Node.js)

### Description
This endpoint demonstrates using Structured Outputs with a Zod schema to extract structured reasoning for a math problem. The model is instructed to act as a math tutor and provide a step-by-step solution.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/responses`

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **model** (string) - Required - The model to use for generation (e.g., `gpt-4o-2024-08-06`).
- **input** (array) - Required - An array of message objects, typically including system and user roles.
  - **role** (string) - Required - The role of the message (e.g., `system`, `user`).
  - **content** (string) - Required - The content of the message.
- **text** (object) - Required - Configuration for text generation.
  - **format** (object) - Required - Specifies the output format.
    - **type** (string) - Required - The type of format, `json_schema` for structured outputs.
    - **name** (string) - Required - A name for the schema, used with `zodTextFormat`.
    - **schema** (object) - Required - The Zod schema object defining the expected structure.
    - **strict** (boolean) - Optional - If true, enforces strict adherence to the schema.

### Request Example
```javascript
import OpenAI from "openai";
import { zodTextFormat } from "openai/helpers/zod";
import { z } from "zod";

const openai = new OpenAI();

const Step = z.object({
  explanation: z.string(),
  output: z.string()
});

const MathReasoning = z.object({
  steps: z.array(Step),
  final_answer: z.string()
});

const response = await openai.responses.parse({
  model: "gpt-4o-2024-08-06",
  input: [
    {
      role: "system",
      content: "You are a helpful math tutor. Guide the user through the solution step by step."
    },
    {
      role: "user",
      content: "how can I solve 8x + 7 = -23"
    }
  ],
  text: {
    format: zodTextFormat(MathReasoning, "math_reasoning")
  }
});

const math_reasoning = response.output_parsed;
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **output_parsed** (object) - The parsed output according to the provided schema.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "steps": [
    {
      "explanation": "Start with the equation 8x + 7 = -23.",
      "output": "8x + 7 = -23"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Subtract 7 from both sides to isolate the term with the variable.",
      "output": "8x = -23 - 7"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Simplify the right side of the equation.",
      "output": "8x = -30"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Divide both sides by 8 to solve for x.",
      "output": "x = -30 / 8"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Simplify the fraction.",
      "output": "x = -15 / 4"
    }
  ],
  "final_answer": "x = -15 / 4"
}
```
```

### Filesystem Routing Examples (JavaScript)

Source: https://vite-plugin-ssr.com/

Illustrates vite-plugin-ssr's filesystem-based routing mechanism. It shows how directory and file names map to URL paths, including dynamic routes. It also presents examples of Route Strings and Route Functions for more flexible routing configurations.

```javascript
// FILESYSTEM
// URL
// pages/index.page.js      => /
// pages/about.page.js      => /about
// pages/faq/index.page.js  => /faq
// pages/movie/@id/index.page.js => /movie/1, /movie/2, /movie/3, ...

// Route String
export default '/movie/@id'

// Route Function — for full flexibility
export default pageContext => pageContext.urlPathname === '/admin' && pageContext.isAdmin
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Create or update an installation with billing plan and notification settings. This endpoint is secured with User Authentication and allows you to configure installation-level billing and manage active notifications.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}

### Description
Create or update an installation with billing plan and notification settings.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

### Request Body
- **billingPlan** (object) - Optional - The billing plan for the installation. If not set, the installation is billed on resource level.
- **notification** (object or null) - Optional - Installation's active notification. Return `null` to remove any current installation notification.

### Request Example
{
  "billingPlan": {},
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Account is exceeding the maximum allowed storage on the current plan"
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the installation
- **notification** (object or null) - Installation's active notification

#### Error Responses
- **400** - Bad Request
- **403** - Forbidden
- **409** - Conflict

### Security
User Authentication required
```

### Basic Astro Middleware Setup (JavaScript)

Source: https://docs.astro.build/en/guides/middleware

This snippet demonstrates the basic setup for Astro middleware in a JavaScript file. It shows how to export an `onRequest` function that accepts `context` and `next`. Inside, it shows how to modify `context.locals` and return the result of `next()` to continue the request handling.

```javascript
export function onRequest (context, next) {
  // intercept data from a request
  // optionally, modify the properties in `locals`
  context.locals.title = "New title";
  // return a Response or the result of calling `next()`
  return next();
};
```

### Enable Multi-Step Tool Calls with stopWhen (TypeScript)

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nodejs

This code configures multi-step tool calls using the `stopWhen` option with `stepCountIs(5)`, allowing the model up to 5 steps to generate a response. It also includes an `onStepFinish` callback to log `toolResults`. This enables the model to use tool outputs for subsequent generations. Dependencies are the same as the previous snippet.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText, tool, stepCountIs } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import { z } from 'zod';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');
    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
      tools: {
        weather: tool({
          description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
          inputSchema: z.object({
            location: z
              .string()
              .describe('The location to get the weather for'),
          }),
          execute: async ({ location }) => {
            const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
            return { location, temperature };
          },
        }),
      },
      stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
      onStepFinish: async ({ toolResults }) => {
        if (toolResults.length) {
          console.log(JSON.stringify(toolResults, null, 2));
        }
      },
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');
    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Vercel config.json: Full Example

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/build-output-api/v3/configuration

A comprehensive example of a config.json file demonstrating the usage of version, routes, images, wildcard domains, overrides, cache, framework, and crons properties.

```json
{
  "version": 3,
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/redirect",
      "status": 308,
      "headers": {
        "Location": "https://example.com/"
      }
    },
    {
      "src": "/blog",
      "dest": "/blog.$wildcard.html"
    }
  ],
  "images": {
    "sizes": [640, 750, 828, 1080, 1200],
    "domains": [],
    "minimumCacheTTL": 60,
    "formats": ["image/avif", "image/webp"],
    "qualities": [25, 50, 75],
    "localPatterns": [
      {
        "pathname": "^/assets/.*$",
        "search": ""
      }
    ],
    "remotePatterns": [
      {
        "protocol": "https",
        "hostname": "^via\\.placeholder\\.com$",
        "port": "",
        "pathname": "^/1280x640/.*$",
        "search": "?v=1"
      }
    ]
  },
  "wildcard": [
    {
      "domain": "example.com",
      "value": "en-US"
    },
    {
      "domain": "example.nl",
      "value": "nl-NL"
    },
    {
      "domain": "example.fr",
      "value": "fr"
    }
  ],
  "overrides": {
    "blog.html": {
      "path": "blog"
    }
  },
  "cache": [
    ".cache/**",
    "node_modules/**"
  ],

    }
  ]
}

### Example Request to Vulnerable Application (HTTP)

Source: https://owasp.org/www-project-web-security-testing-guide/latest/4-Web_Application_Security_Testing/11-Client-side_Testing/07-Testing_Cross_Origin_Resource_Sharing

This HTTP GET request targets a vulnerable resource (`profile.php`) which is then used in an XSS attack. The `Host` and `Referer` headers are crucial in understanding the context of the request.

```http
GET /profile.php HTTP/1.1
Host: example.foo
...
Referer: https://example.foo/main.php
Connection: keep-alive
```

### Get Resource

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Retrieves details for a specific resource within a Vercel installation. This endpoint is secured using System Authentication.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}

### Description
Get a Resource

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resources/{resourceId}`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"
- **resourceId** (string) - Required - Partner-provided resource ID

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the resource. If not set, the resource is billed on installation level.
  - **id** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID of the resource
  - **metadata** (object) - Required - User-inputted metadata based on the registered metadata schema.
  - **name** (string) - Required - User-inputted name for the resource.
  - **notification** (object) - Resource's active notification. Example: { "level": "warn", "title": "Database is nearing maximum planned size" }
    - **productId** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product. Example: "redis"
    - **protocolSettings** (object)
    - **status** (string) - Required - One of: `ready` | `pending` | `onboarding` | `suspended` | `resumed` | `uninstalled` | `error`

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "billingPlan": {
    "id": "some_plan_id",
    "metadata": {},
    "name": "Example Plan",
    "notification": {
      "level": "warn",
      "title": "Database is nearing maximum planned size"
    },
    "productId": "redis",
    "protocolSettings": {},
    "status": "ready"
  }
}
```
```

### Stream Text from AI Model (TypeScript)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/ai-gateway/getting-started

This TypeScript code snippet demonstrates how to use the Vercel AI SDK to stream text from an AI model. It imports necessary functions, loads environment variables, defines an async function to make the request, and iterates over the streamed text output.

```typescript
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';

async function main() {
  const result = streamText({
    model: 'openai/gpt-5',
    prompt: 'Invent a new holiday and describe its traditions.',
  });

  for await (const textPart of result.textStream) {
    process.stdout.write(textPart);
  }
  console.log();
  console.log('Token usage:', await result.usage);
  console.log('Finish reason:', await result.finishReason);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Update Custom Server with Vite Middleware (Express Example)

Source: https://remix.run/docs/en/main/future/vite

Adapt your custom server (e.g., Express) to use Vite's connect middleware for handling asset and SSR requests during development. This example shows how to integrate Vite's dev server with an Express application.

```javascript
import { createRequestHandler } from "@remix-run/express";
import { installGlobals } from "@remix-run/node";
import express from "express";

installGlobals();

const viteDevServer = process.env.NODE_ENV === "production" ? undefined : await import("vite").then((vite) => vite.createServer({
  server: {
    middlewareMode: true,
  },
}));

const app = express();

// handle asset requests
if (viteDevServer) {
  app.use(viteDevServer.middlewares);
} else {
  app.use(
    "/assets",
    express.static("build/client/assets", {
      immutable: true,
      maxAge: "1y",
    })
  );
}
app.use(express.static("build/client", { maxAge: "1h" }));

// handle SSR requests
app.all(
  "*",
  createRequestHandler({
    build: viteDevServer ? () => viteDevServer.ssrLoadModule(
      "virtual:remix/server-build"
    ) : await import("./build/server/index.js"),
  })
);

const port = 3000;
app.listen(port, () => console.log("http://localhost:" + port));
```

### SvelteKit 'handle' Hook Logic Example (TypeScript)

Source: https://kit.svelte.dev/docs/hooks

This TypeScript example illustrates the core logic within a SvelteKit 'handle' hook. It checks if the request path starts with '/custom' and returns a custom response; otherwise, it proceeds with the default SvelteKit resolution. This demonstrates conditional response handling.

```typescript
export const handle: Handle = async ({ event, resolve }) => {
  if (event.url.pathname.startsWith('/custom')) {
    return new Response('custom response');
  }
  const response = await resolve(event);
  return response;
};
```

### LZ78 Dictionary Building and Output Example

Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LZ77_and_LZ78

Demonstrates the step-by-step process of building an LZ78 dictionary for a given sequence of tokens and the resulting compressed output. It highlights how the algorithm greedily adds entries and outputs references.

```pseudocode
Initialize last_matching_index = 0, next_available_index = 1
Initialize dictionary = { 0: {index: null, token: null} }

For each token in input_stream:
  If {last_matching_index, token} exists in dictionary:
    last_matching_index = dictionary[{last_matching_index, token}].index
  Else:
    Create new dictionary entry: dictionary[next_available_index] = {index: last_matching_index, token: token}
    Output last_matching_index
    Output token
    last_matching_index = 0
    Increment next_available_index

// Handle remaining sequence or EOF marker
```

### Node.js Dockerfile for Application Deployment

Source: https://hono.dev/docs/getting-started/nodejs

A multi-stage Dockerfile designed for building and running a Node.js application. It first installs dependencies, builds the project, and then creates a leaner production image. It includes user and group setup for security and exposes port 3000.

```dockerfile
FROM node:22-alpine AS base
FROM base AS builder
RUN apk add --no-cache gcompat
WORKDIR /app
COPY package*json tsconfig.json src ./
RUN npm ci && \
    npm run build && \
    npm prune --production
FROM base AS runner
WORKDIR /app
RUN addgroup --system --gid 1001 nodejs
RUN adduser --system --uid 1001 hono
COPY --from=builder --chown=hono:nodejs /app/node_modules /app/node_modules
COPY --from=builder --chown=hono:nodejs /app/dist /app/dist
COPY --from=builder --chown=hono:nodejs /app/package.json /app/package.json
USER hono
EXPOSE 3000
CMD ["node", "/app/dist/index.js"]
```

--------------------------------

### Perform HTTP GET Request with Node.js

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/http.html

This example illustrates how to use the http.get method in Node.js to fetch data from a specified URL. It includes a callback function to handle the response, checking the status code and content type. The example shows how to process JSON data received from the server.

```javascript
http.get('http://localhost:8000/', (res) => {
  const { statusCode } = res;
  const contentType = res.headers['content-type'];

  let error;
  // Any 2xx status code signifies a successful response
  if (statusCode !== 200) {
    error = new Error('Request Failed.\n' + `Status Code: ${statusCode}`);
  } else if (!/^application\/json/.test(contentType)) {
    error = new Error('Invalid content-type.\n' + `Expected application/json but received ${contentType}`);
  }

  if (error) {
    console.error(error.message);
    // Consume response data to free up memory
    res.resume();
    return;
  }

  res.setEncoding('utf8');
  let rawData = '';
  res.on('data', (chunk) => { rawData += chunk; });
  res.on('end', () => {
    try {
      const parsedData = JSON.parse(rawData);
      console.log(parsedData);
    } catch (e) {
      console.error(e.message);
    }
  });
}).on('error', (e) => {
  console.error(`Got error: ${e.message}`);
});
```

### Storefront API Client Example (Shopify API SDK)

Source: https://shopify.dev/docs/api/storefront

Illustrates using the `shopify.clients.Storefront` client to query products with an access token.

```APIDOC
## Shopify API Storefront Client (JavaScript SDK)

### Description
Uses the official Shopify API JavaScript SDK to create a Storefront client and query for products.

### Method
N/A (SDK client method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Request Body (for `client.query`)
- **data** (String) - Required - The GraphQL query string.

### Request Example
```javascript
// Load the access token as per instructions above
const storefrontAccessToken = '';
// Shop from which we're fetching data
const shop = 'my-shop.myshopify.com';

// StorefrontClient takes in the shop url and the Storefront Access Token for that shop.
const storefrontClient = new shopify.clients.Storefront({
  domain: shop,
  storefrontAccessToken,
});

// Use client.query and pass your query as `data`
const products = await storefrontClient.query({
  data: `{
    products (first: 3) {
      edges {
        node {
          id
          title
        }
      }
    }
  `,
});
```

### Response
#### Success Response
- **products** (Object) - The result of the GraphQL query, containing product data.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "products": {
    "edges": [
      {
        "node": {
          "id": "gid://shopify/Product/1234567890",
          "title": "Sample Product 1"
        }
      }
      // ... more products
    ]
  }
}
```
```

### Using Nitro KV Storage

Source: https://nitro.unjs.io/guide/storage

Demonstrates basic usage of Nitro's storage layer for getting and setting items. It shows default in-memory storage, specifying a base, and using data storage for persistent writes.

```javascript
await useStorage().setItem('test:foo', { hello: 'world' })
await useStorage().getItem('test:foo')

// Specify base
await useStorage('test').setItem('foo', { hello: 'world' })

// Use data storage for persistent writes
const dataStorage = useStorage('data')
await dataStorage.setItem('test', 'works')
await dataStorage.getItem('data:test')

// Using generics for type safety
await useStorage<{ hello: string }>('test').getItem('foo')
await useStorage('test').getItem<{ hello: string }>('foo')
```

### HTTP GET Request for Protected Resource Metadata (With Path)

Source: https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9728

This example shows an HTTP GET request for protected resource metadata when the resource identifier includes a path component. The URL construction involves removing any trailing slash from the host and inserting the well-known URI suffix before the resource's path.

```http
GET /.well-known/oauth-protected-resource/resource1 HTTP/1.1
Host: resource.example.com
```

### URI Component Example Breakdown

Source: https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc3986

Demonstrates two complete URI examples with their constituent parts labeled: scheme, authority, path, query, and fragment. The first example shows an HTTP-style URI with port number; the second shows a URN-style URI.

```URI
foo://example.com:8042/over/there?name=ferret#nose
\_/ \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_/\_\_\_\_\_\_\_/ \_\_\_\_\_\_\_/ \_\_/
| | | | |
scheme authority path query fragment

urn:example:animal:ferret:nose
```

### GET /api/data - Example Response with Vary Header

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/edge-cache

This example demonstrates a Vercel Function that returns a JSON response and sets the `Vary` and `Cache-Control` headers. The `Vary` header ensures that the cache is segmented based on the incoming request's country, and `Cache-Control` sets the maximum time the response can be cached by the CDN.

```APIDOC
## GET /api/data

### Description
Returns a JSON response with caching headers configured for Vercel's Edge Network. The response is cacheable based on the `X-Vercel-IP-Country` header and has a `s-maxage` of 1 hour.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/api/data

### Parameters

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Request Example
```json
{
  "message": "Hello from the United States!"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **data** (string) - A message indicating the response is variable by country.
- **headers** (object) - Contains `Cache-Control` and `Vary` headers.
  - **Cache-Control** (string) - `s-maxage=3600` (1 hour)
  - **Vary** (string) - `X-Vercel-IP-Country`

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "data": "This response varies by country"
}
```

```typescript
// Next.js (/app) or Other frameworks
import { type NextRequest } from 'next/server';

export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {
  return Response.json(
    {
      data: 'This response varies by country'
    },
    {
      status: 200,
      headers: {
        'Cache-Control': 's-maxage=3600',
        'Vary': 'X-Vercel-IP-Country',
      },
    }
  );
}
```
```

### PCRE *COMMIT Verb Example

Source: https://www.pcre.org/original/doc/html/pcrepattern.html

Demonstrates the *COMMIT verb, which forces the entire match to fail if backtracking reaches it after a later failure. It prevents further matching attempts by advancing the starting point. The example 'a+(*COMMIT)b' matches 'xxaab' but not 'aacaab', acting as a dynamic anchor.

```regex
(\*COMMIT)
```

```regex
a+(\*COMMIT)b
```

```regex
/(\*COMMIT)abc/
```

### Get Integration Resource

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Fetches a specific resource by its partner-provided ID for a given integration installation. Requires integrationConfigurationId and resourceId as path parameters. Secured using a bearer token.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{integrationConfigurationId}/resources/{resourceId}

### Description
Get a resource by its partner ID.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{integrationConfigurationId}/resources/{resourceId}`

### Security
Use bearer token to secure this endpoint.

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **integrationConfigurationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the integration configuration (installation) the resource belongs to
- **resourceId** (string) - Required - The ID provided by the 3rd party provider for the given resource

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **billingPlanId** (string) - The ID of the billing plan the resource is subscribed to, if applicable
- **id** (string) - Required - The ID provided by the 3rd party provider for the given resource
- **internalId** (string) - Required - The ID assigned by Vercel for the given resource
- **metadata** (object) - The configured metadata for the resource as defined by its product's Metadata Schema
- **name** (string) - Required - The name of the resource as it is recorded in Vercel
- **notification** (object) - The notification, if set, displayed to the user when viewing the resource in Vercel
  - **productId** (string) - Required - The ID of the product the resource is derived from
- **protocolSettings** (object) - Any settings provided for the resource to support its product's protocols
- **status** (string) - One of: `ready` | `pending` | `onboarding` | `suspended` | `resumed` | `uninstalled` | `error` - The current status of the resource
```

### Create a LangChain Agent with TypeScript

Source: https://js.langchain.com/

This example demonstrates how to create a basic agent using LangChain in TypeScript. It defines a tool to get weather information and then creates an agent that can use this tool to respond to user queries.

```typescript
import * as z from "zod"; // npm install @langchain/anthropic to call the model
import { createAgent, tool } from "langchain";

const getWeather = tool(
  ({ city }) => `It's always sunny in ${city}!`,
  {
    name: "get_weather",
    description: "Get the weather for a given city",
    schema: z.object({
      city: z.string(),
    }),
  }
);

const agent = createAgent({
  model: "claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929",
  tools: [getWeather],
});

console.log(
  await agent.invoke({
    messages: [{ role: "user", content: "What's the weather in Tokyo?" }],
  })
);
```

### Example CSS File Transformation in Vite Development

Source: https://remix.run/docs/en/main/future/vite

Shows how a simple CSS file is transformed into JavaScript code by Vite during development to enable HMR and lazy-loading of styles. This transformation is not present in production builds.

```javascript
import {createHotContext as __vite__createHotContext} from "/@vite/client";
import.meta.hot = __vite__createHotContext("/app/styles.css");
import {updateStyle as __vite__updateStyle, removeStyle as __vite__removeStyle} from "/@vite/client";

const __vite__id = "/path/to/app/styles.css";
const __vite__css = "*{margin:0}" 
__vite__updateStyle(__vite__id, __vite__css);

import.meta.hot.accept();
import.meta.hot.prune(()=>__vite__removeStyle(__vite__id));
```

### Process Data Chunks in API Endpoint (Node.js)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

This guide demonstrates how to create a serverless API endpoint on Vercel that processes data in chunks. This is essential for handling large uploads or streaming data efficiently without exceeding memory limits. The example uses Node.js streams.

```javascript
import type { VercelRequest, VercelResponse } from '@vercel/node';

export default async (request: VercelRequest, response: VercelResponse) => {
  if (request.method === 'POST') {
    let requestBody = '';

    request.on('data', (chunk) => {
      requestBody += chunk.toString(); // Process chunk
      // In a real scenario, you might append to a buffer or stream to disk
    });

    request.on('end', () => {
      try {
        // Process the complete requestBody here
        console.log('Received data chunks, processing complete.');
        response.status(200).json({ message: 'Data processed successfully', receivedDataLength: requestBody.length });
      } catch (error) {
        console.error('Error processing data:', error);
        response.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to process data' });
      }
    });

    request.on('error', (error) => {
      console.error('Request error:', error);
      response.status(500).json({ error: 'Request error occurred' });
    });

  } else {
    response.status(405).json({ error: 'Method Not Allowed' });
  }
};
```

### Get Deployment Events - TypeScript Example

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/rest-api/reference/endpoints/deployments/get-deployment-events

This TypeScript code snippet demonstrates how to use the Vercel SDK to fetch deployment events. It shows how to instantiate the Vercel client and call the `getDeploymentEvents` method with various parameters to filter and retrieve specific event data. The `bearerToken` is required for authentication.

```typescript
import { Vercel } from "@vercel/sdk";
const vercel = new Vercel({ bearerToken: "", });
async function run() {
  const result = await vercel.deployments.getDeploymentEvents({
    idOrUrl: "dpl_5WJWYSyB7BpgTj3EuwF37WMRBXBtPQ2iTMJHJBJyRfd",
    direction: "backward",
    follow: 1,
    limit: 100,
    name: "bld_cotnkcr76",
    since: 1540095775941,
    until: 1540106318643,
    statusCode: "5xx",
    delimiter: 1,
    builds: 1,
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug",
  });
  console.log(result);
}
run();
```
