### Next.js App Router Example

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/storage/vercel-blob/using-blob-sdk

An example of how to implement client uploads using `handleUpload` within a Next.js App Router route handler.

```APIDOC
## POST /api/post/upload

### Description
Handles incoming POST requests for file uploads using the Vercel Blob `handleUpload` function within a Next.js App Router.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/api/post/upload`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **body** (HandleUploadBody) - Required - The parsed JSON request body containing upload details.

### Request Example
```json
// This is conceptually what the request body might look like after parsing
{
  "//": "This is an example, the actual body is parsed from the request"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **jsonResponse** (object) - The response from `handleUpload`, which can be a client token or an upload completion confirmation.

#### Error Response (400)
- **error** (object) - An error object containing a message if the upload fails.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "type": "blob.generate-client-token",
  "clientToken": "<generated_token>"
}
```

#### Code Example (Next.js App Router)
```javascript
import { handleUpload, type HandleUploadBody } from '@vercel/blob/client';
import { NextResponse } from 'next/server';

export async function POST(request: Request): Promise<NextResponse> {
  const body = (await request.json()) as HandleUploadBody;
  try {
    const jsonResponse = await handleUpload({
      body,
      request,
      onBeforeGenerateToken: async (pathname, clientPayload) => {
        // Authenticate and authorize users here
        // Validate clientPayload for security
        return {
          allowedContentTypes: [
            'image/jpeg',
            'image/png',
            'image/webp',
            'text/*'
          ],
          // callbackUrl: 'https://example.com/api/avatar/upload'
        };
      },
      onUploadCompleted: async ({ blob, tokenPayload }) => {
        console.log('blob upload completed', blob, tokenPayload);
        try {
          // Update your database with the blob URL
        } catch (error) {
          throw new Error('Could not update post');
        }
      },
    });
    return NextResponse.json(jsonResponse);
  } catch (error) {
    return NextResponse.json(
      {
        error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
      },
      { status: 400 }
    );
  }
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### List Billing Plans For Installation

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Returns the set of billing plans available to a specific Installation.

```APIDOC
## GET /v1/installations/{installationId}/plans

### Description
Returns the set of billing plans available to a specific Installation.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/v1/installations/{installationId}/plans

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **plans** (array) - Required - Description of the billing plans available.
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Provision a new resource within an installation. This synchronous operation returns the newly provisioned resource with its secrets and configuration details.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

### Description
Provisions a Resource. This is a synchronous operation but the provisioning can be asynchronous as the Resource does not need to be immediately available. However, the secrets must be known ahead of time.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resources`

### Security
User Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

#### Request Body
- **id** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID of the resource
- **productId** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product. Example: "redis"
- **name** (string) - Required - User-inputted name for the resource
- **metadata** (object) - Required - User-inputted metadata based on the registered metadata schema
- **secrets** (array) - Required - Resource secrets and credentials
- **protocolSettings** (object) - Optional - Protocol-specific settings
- **billingPlan** (object) - Optional - The billing plan for the resource. If not set, the resource is billed on installation level.

### Request Example
{
  "id": "res_123456",
  "productId": "redis",
  "name": "primary-cache",
  "metadata": {
    "region": "us-east-1"
  },
  "secrets": [
    {
      "key": "connection_string",
      "value": "redis://..."
    }
  ]
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **id** (string) - The partner-specific ID of the resource
- **productId** (string) - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product
- **name** (string) - User-inputted name for the resource
- **metadata** (object) - User-inputted metadata
- **status** (string) - One of: `ready` | `pending` | `onboarding` | `suspended` | `resumed` | `uninstalled` | `error`
- **secrets** (array) - Resource secrets
- **billingPlan** (object) - The billing plan for the resource
- **notification** (object) - Resource's active notification

#### Response Example
{
  "id": "res_123456",
  "productId": "redis",
  "name": "primary-cache",
  "status": "ready",
  "metadata": {
    "region": "us-east-1"
  },
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Database is nearing maximum planned size"
  }
}

#### Error Responses
- **400** - Bad Request
- **403** - Forbidden
- **409** - Conflict
```

--------------------------------

### Example: OG Image Styling with Tailwind CSS (Experimental)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/functions/og-image-generation

This example shows how to use Tailwind CSS for styling OG images. Note that this feature is experimental. You need to configure Tailwind CSS in your project and ensure the necessary packages are installed. This allows for utility-first CSS class names within your JSX.

```javascript
import { ImageResponse } from '@vercel/og';

export default async function handler(req) {
  return new ImageResponse(
    (
      <div
        style={{
          display: 'flex',
          width: '100%',
          height: '100%',
          alignItems: 'center',
          justifyContent: 'center',
          fontSize: '64px',
          fontWeight: 'bold',
          color: '#ffffff',
          background: 'linear-gradient(135deg, #667eea 0%, #764ba2 100%)',
          textShadow: '4px 4px 8px rgba(0,0,0,0.5)',
        }}
        tw="flex items-center justify-center"
      >
        <h1 tw="text-6xl font-bold text-white text-shadow-lg">Tailwind CSS OG</h1>
      </div>
    ),
    {
      width: 1200,
      height: 630,
      // Tailwind CSS requires specific font setup if not using system fonts
      // Refer to @vercel/og documentation for detailed Tailwind CSS integration
    },
  );
}
```

### DNS Zone Configuration Example (BIND)

Source: https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/rfc9460

This example demonstrates a typical DNS zone configuration using BIND syntax. It includes CNAME records for aliasing services and SVCB records for specifying service parameters like target names and keys.

```dns
$ORIGIN example.com.
; Origin
foo 3600 IN CNAME foosvc.example.net.
_8080._foo.foo 3600 IN CNAME foosvc.example.net.
bar 300 IN AAAA 2001:db8::2
_9090._bar.bar 3600 IN SVCB 1 bar key65444=...
$ORIGIN example.net.
; Service provider zone
foosvc 3600 IN SVCB 1 . key65333=...
foosvc 300 IN AAAA 2001:db8::1
```

### Corepack Utility Command Examples

```bash

# Clear the Corepack cache directory
corepack cache clean

# Enable shims for yarn and pnpm
corepack enable yarn pnpm

# Install the package manager defined in the local project
corepack install

# Globally install a specific version of yarn
corepack install -g yarn@3.2.3

# Pack the current project's package manager for offline use
corepack pack -o ./my-package-manager.tar.gz
```

### Make First API Request (Text Generation)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/

This snippet shows how to make a basic API request to generate text using the 'gpt-5.1' model. It requires an API key for authentication and takes a text prompt as input, returning the generated text output. This is a fundamental operation for most applications using the OpenAI API.

```curl
curl https://api.openai.com/v1/responses \
-H "Content-Type: application/json" \
-H "Authorization: Bearer $OPENAI_API_KEY" \
-d '{ "model": "gpt-5.1", "input": "Write a short bedtime story about a unicorn." }'
```

```javascript
import OpenAI from "openai";

const client = new OpenAI();

const response = await client.responses.create({
  model: "gpt-5.1",
  input: "Write a short bedtime story about a unicorn.",
});

console.log(response.output_text);
```

```python
from openai import OpenAI

client = OpenAI()

response = client.responses.create(
  model="gpt-5.1",
  input="Write a short bedtime story about a unicorn."
)

print(response.output_text)
```

```csharp
using OpenAI.Responses;

string apiKey = Environment.GetEnvironmentVariable("OPENAI_API_KEY")!;
var client = new OpenAIResponseClient(model: "gpt-5.1", apiKey: apiKey);

OpenAIResponse response = client.CreateResponse(
  "Write a short bedtime story about a unicorn."
);

Console.WriteLine(response.GetOutputText());
```

### Server Assets Retrieval Example

Source: https://nitro.unjs.io/guide/assets

Assets in the `server/assets/` directory are bundled into the server. They can be accessed using the `assets:server` mount point via the storage layer. Be mindful of asset size to avoid bloating the server bundle.

```typescript
export default defineEventHandler(async () => {
  const data = await useStorage('assets:server').getItem(`data.json`)
  return data
})

### GET /app/api/hello/route.ts

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/functions/functions-api-reference

Basic Vercel Function example that returns a simple text response. This demonstrates the fundamental structure of a function using the Web Handler pattern with the Request API.

```APIDOC
## GET /app/api/hello/route.ts

### Description
A basic Vercel Function that responds to GET requests with a simple text message.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
app/api/hello/route.ts

### Function Signature
Vercel Functions use a Web Handler pattern with the following parameters:

| Parameter | Type | Description | Framework Support |
|-----------|------|-------------|-------------------|
| request | Request | An instance of the Request object (NextRequest in Next.js) | All frameworks |
| context | Object | Deprecated - use @vercel/functions instead | Other frameworks |

### Request Example
```typescript
export function GET(request: Request) {
  return new Response('Hello from Vercel!');
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **body** (string) - "Hello from Vercel!"

### Response Example
```
Hello from Vercel!
```
```

### Filter Requests with WHERE Clause

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/observability/monitoring/quickstart

The WHERE clause allows you to specify conditions for filtering data. This example filters requests to include only those from 'my-site.com' and whose path starts with '/posts'. The '%' acts as a wildcard for any characters following '/posts'.

```text
host = 'my-site.com' and like(request_path, '/posts%')
```

### Microfrontends JSON Configuration Example

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/microfrontends/quickstart

Defines the structure for microfrontend applications, including fallback URLs for development and routing rules for specific paths. This JSON file is essential for Vercel to manage and route requests to different microfrontend applications.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://openapi.vercel.sh/microfrontends.json",
  "applications": {
    "web": {
      "development": {
        "fallback": "TODO: a URL in production that should be used for requests to apps not running locally"
      }
    },
    "docs": {
      "routing": [
        {
          "group": "docs",
          "paths": ["/docs/:path*"]
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

### Node.js Callback Handler with HTTP Request

Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/nodejs-handler.html

An example of a Node.js Lambda function using the callback pattern to make an HTTP GET request and return the status code. It demonstrates error handling using the callback.

```javascript
import https from "https";
let url = "https://aws.amazon.com/";
export const handler = (event, context, callback) => {
  https.get(url, (res) => {
    callback(null, res.statusCode);
  }).on("error", (e) => {
    callback(Error(e));
  });
};
```

### Serve TLS HTTP Connections (Go)

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Accepts incoming TLS connections on the provided Listener and serves HTTP requests. It performs TLS setup for each connection before reading and handling requests via the server's Handler. Certificate and key files are required unless TLSConfig.Certificates, TLSConfig.GetCertificate, or config.GetConfigForClient are populated. ServeTLS returns a non-nil error and closes the listener upon completion or after Server.Shutdown/Close.

```go
func (s *Server) ServeTLS(l net.Listener, certFile, keyFile string) error
```

### Delete Headers Starting with Prefix for /home Route (JSON)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/project-configuration

This example shows how to delete any incoming request header that begins with the prefix 'x-react-router-' for all requests to the '/home' route using Vercel's JSON configuration.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://openapi.vercel.sh/vercel.json",
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/home",
      "transforms": [
        {
          "type": "request.headers",
          "op": "delete",
          "target": {
            "key": {
              "pre": "x-react-router-"
            }
          }
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Provision a new resource within an installation. This synchronous operation returns resource details including secrets immediately, though actual provisioning may be asynchronous. Requires User Authentication.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resources

### Description
Provision a new resource. This is a synchronous operation that returns secrets immediately.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resources`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

### Request Body
- **productId** (string) - Required - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product. Example: "redis"
- **name** (string) - Required - User-inputted name for the resource
- **metadata** (object) - Required - User-inputted metadata based on the registered metadata schema
- **billingPlan** (object) - Optional - The billing plan for the resource. If not set, billed on installation level

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **id** (string) - The partner-specific ID of the resource
- **productId** (string) - The partner-specific ID/slug of the product
- **name** (string) - User-inputted name for the resource
- **metadata** (object) - User-inputted metadata
- **status** (string) - One of: `ready` | `pending` | `onboarding` | `suspended` | `resumed` | `uninstalled` | `error`
- **secrets** (array) - Resource secrets
- **notification** (object) - Resource's active notification

#### Response Example
{
  "id": "resource-123",
  "productId": "redis",
  "name": "My Redis Instance",
  "status": "ready",
  "secrets": [],
  "notification": {
    "level": "warn",
    "title": "Database is nearing maximum planned size"
  }
}

#### Error Responses

- **403** - Forbidden
- **409** - Conflict

### Push Serialized Items to SitecoreAI Local Environment using .NET CLI

Source: https://doc.sitecore.com/xmc/en/developers/xm-cloud/walkthrough--setting-up-your-full-stack-xm-cloud-local-development-environment.html

This command pushes serialized items from your local repository to the specified SitecoreAI local environment. It uses the connection details configured in `.sitecore/user.json`. Note that this command does not publish items; manual publishing is required afterward. Ensure the local environment name (`-n`) is correctly specified.

```bash
dotnet sitecore ser push -n "local"
```

### POST /app/installations/{INSTALLATION_ID}/access_tokens

Source: https://docs.github.com/en/apps/creating-github-apps/authenticating-with-a-github-app/generating-an-installation-access-token-for-a-github-app

Creates an installation access token for a GitHub App installation. This token can be used to authenticate API requests on behalf of the installation. You can optionally scope the token to specific repositories and permissions.

```APIDOC
## POST /app/installations/{INSTALLATION_ID}/access_tokens

### Description
Generates an installation access token for a GitHub App installation. The token can be scoped to specific repositories and permissions, and expires after 1 hour.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`https://api.github.com/app/installations/{INSTALLATION_ID}/access_tokens`

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **INSTALLATION_ID** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation for which to create an access token

#### Request Body
- **repositories** (array of strings) - Optional - List of repository names to grant access to. Maximum 500 repositories. If not specified, token has access to all repositories the installation was granted access to
- **repository_ids** (array of integers) - Optional - List of repository IDs to grant access to. Maximum 500 repositories. If not specified, token has access to all repositories the installation was granted access to
- **permissions** (object) - Optional - Permissions to grant the token. If not specified, token inherits all permissions granted to the app

### Headers
- **Authorization** (string) - Required - Must be `Bearer {JWT}` where JWT is your JSON web token
- **Accept** (string) - Required - Must be `application/vnd.github+json`
- **X-GitHub-Api-Version** (string) - Required - API version, e.g., `2022-11-28`

### Request Example
```bash
curl --request POST \
  --url "https://api.github.com/app/installations/INSTALLATION_ID/access_tokens" \
  --header "Accept: application/vnd.github+json" \
  --header "Authorization: Bearer JWT" \
  --header "X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28"
```

### Response
#### Success Response (201)
- **token** (string) - The installation access token
- **expires_at** (string) - ISO 8601 timestamp when the token expires (1 hour from creation)
- **permissions** (object) - The permissions granted to the token
- **repositories** (array of objects) - List of repositories the token can access (if scoped)
- **repository_selection** (string) - Either "all" or "selected" indicating scope

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "token": "ghu_16C7e42F292c6912E7710c838347Ae178B4a",
  "expires_at": "2025-01-08T20:30:00Z",
  "permissions": {
    "contents": "read",
    "issues": "write"
  },
  "repositories": [
    {
      "id": 1296269,
      "name": "Hello-World",
      "full_name": "octocat/Hello-World"
    }
  ],
  "repository_selection": "selected"
}
```

### Notes
- The installation access token expires after 1 hour
- The token cannot be granted access to repositories the installation was not granted access to
- The token cannot be granted permissions the app was not granted
- Maximum of 500 repositories can be specified in the request
- Use `Authorization: Bearer` format when passing a JWT (not `Authorization: token`)
```

### Storefront API Client Example (JavaScript)

Source: https://shopify.dev/docs/api/storefront

Demonstrates using the Storefront API client to fetch a specific product by its handle.

```APIDOC
## Storefront API Client (JavaScript)

### Description
Uses a Storefront API client to fetch a single product by its handle, including its ID, title, and handle.

### Method
N/A (Client-side method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **query** (String) - The GraphQL query string.
- **variables** (Object) - An object containing variables for the query.
  - **handle** (String) - The product handle to query.

### Request Example
```javascript
const productQuery = `
  query ProductQuery($handle: String) {
    product(handle: $handle) {
      id
      title
      handle
    }
  }
`;

const { data, errors, extensions } = await client.request(productQuery, {
  variables: {
    handle: 'sample-product',
  },
});
```

### Response
#### Success Response
- **data** (Object) - The data returned from the GraphQL query.
  - **product** (Object) - Details of the requested product.
    - **id** (ID) - The product's unique identifier.
    - **title** (String) - The product's title.
    - **handle** (String) - The product's handle.
- **errors** (Array) - An array of errors, if any occurred.
- **extensions** (Object) - Additional information about the request.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "data": {
    "product": {
      "id": "gid://shopify/Product/1234567890",
      "title": "Sample Product",
      "handle": "sample-product"
    }
  },
  "errors": null,
  "extensions": {
    "cost": {
      "requestedQueryCost": 1,
      "actualQueryCost": 1,
      "throttleStatus": {
        "timeoutApplied": false
      }
    }
  }
}
```
```

### Chat UI with Tool Rendering - Svelte

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/svelte

Svelte component that initializes a Chat instance, handles message submission, and renders both text and tool-specific parts (weather and temperature conversion). Displays tool calls and results in JSON format.

```svelte
<script>
  import { Chat } from '@ai-sdk/svelte';
  let input = '';
  const chat = new Chat({});
  
  function handleSubmit(event: SubmitEvent) {
    event.preventDefault();
    chat.sendMessage({ text: input });
    input = '';
  }
</script>

{#each chat.messages as message, messageIndex (messageIndex)}
  <div>{message.role}</div>
  {#each message.parts as part, partIndex (partIndex)}
    {#if part.type === 'text'}
      <p>{part.text}</p>
    {:else if part.type === 'tool-weather' || part.type === 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius'}
      <pre>{JSON.stringify(part, null, 2)}</pre>
    {/if}
  {/each}
{/each}

<form on:submit={handleSubmit}>
  <input bind:value={input} />
  <button type="submit">Send</button>
</form>
```

### Deploy Puppeteer with Next.js for Web Page Screenshots on Vercel

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/nextjs-prisma-postgres

This guide demonstrates setting up Puppeteer with Next.js on Vercel for headless browser automation. It includes a practical example for efficiently generating web page screenshots. Dependencies include Next.js and Puppeteer. The output is a generated screenshot image.

```javascript
import puppeteer from 'puppeteer';

export default async (req, res) => {
  const browser = await puppeteer.launch({
    args: ['--no-sandbox', '--disable-setuid-sandbox']
  });
  const page = await browser.newPage();
  await page.goto('https://example.com'); // Replace with your target URL
  const screenshot = await page.screenshot();
  await browser.close();

  res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'image/png');
  res.send(screenshot);
};
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Creates a resource transfer request to prepare transferring resources from the current installation to a new one. The target installation will be determined during the verify and accept steps.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests

### Description
Create Resources Transfer Request - Prepares to transfer resources from the current installation to a new one

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests`

### Security
System Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the source installation to transfer resources from. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **providerClaimId** (string) - Required - The provider-specific claim ID for the resource transfer

#### Response Codes
- 200 - Success
- 400 - Bad Request
- 403 - Forbidden
- 409 - Conflict
- 422 - Unprocessable Entity
```

### TypeScript SDK: Initialize Client and Search

Source: https://docs.perplexity.ai/

This TypeScript example shows how to initialize the Perplexity client and perform a search. It mirrors the Python functionality, demonstrating how to integrate Perplexity's search capabilities into a TypeScript application.

```typescript
import Perplexity from '@perplexity/perplexity-js';

const client = new Perplexity({
  apiKey: 'YOUR_API_KEY',
});

async function performSearch() {
  const query = [
    'What is the weather like today?',
    'Latest tech news',
  ];
  try {
    const searchResults = await client.search.create({
      query: query,
    });
    searchResults.results.forEach((result) => {
      console.log(`${result.title}: ${result.url}`);
    });
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error performing search:', error);
  }
}

performSearch();
```

### Router-Level Middleware Implementation

Source: https://expressjs.com/en/guide/using-middleware.html

Demonstrates comprehensive router-level middleware setup including unconditional middleware, sub-stacks for specific paths, and conditional routing. This example shows how to create a router instance, apply middleware at different levels, and handle special cases like skipping routes based on parameters.

```javascript
const express = require('express')
const app = express()
const router = express.Router()

// a middleware function with no mount path. This code is executed for every request to the router
router.use((req, res, next) => {
  console.log('Time:', Date.now())
  next()
})

// a middleware sub-stack shows request info for any type of HTTP request to the /user/:id path
router.use('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  console.log('Request URL:', req.originalUrl)
  next()
}, (req, res, next) => {
  console.log('Request Type:', req.method)
  next()
})

// a middleware sub-stack that handles GET requests to the /user/:id path
router.get('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  // if the user ID is 0, skip to the next router
  if (req.params.id === '0') next('route')
  // otherwise pass control to the next middleware function in this stack
  else next()
}, (req, res, next) => {
  // render a regular page
  res.render('regular')
})

// handler for the /user/:id path, which renders a special page
router.get('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  console.log(req.params.id)
  res.render('special')
})

// mount the router on the app
app.use('/', router)
```

### Legacy Routes to Modern Configuration Migration

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/project-configuration

Guide for migrating from legacy routes property to modern rewrites, redirects, and headers configuration. Shows equivalent configurations using the new approach.

```APIDOC
## Legacy Routes to Modern Configuration Migration

### Key Differences

#### Pattern Matching
**Legacy (routes)**: Dots must be escaped with two backslashes in PCRE Regex
```json
{
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/atom\\\\.xml",
      "dest": "/api/rss"
    }
  ]
}
```

**Modern (rewrites)**: Dots do not need escaping
```json
{
  "rewrites": [
    {
      "source": "/atom.xml",
      "destination": "/api/rss"
    }
  ]
}
```

#### Continuing Matches
**Legacy (routes)**: Use `"continue": true` to apply multiple rules
```json
{
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/favicon.ico",
      "headers": { "Cache-Control": "public, max-age=3600" },
      "continue": true
    }
  ]
}
```

**Modern (headers)**: Multiple rules apply by default
```json
{
  "headers": [
    {
      "source": "/favicon.ico",
      "headers": [
        {
          "key": "Cache-Control",
          "value": "public, max-age=3600"
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

#### Filesystem Precedence
**Legacy (routes)**: Use `"handle": "filesystem"` to check filesystem first
```json
{
  "routes": [
    { "handle": "filesystem" },
    { "src": "/(.*)", "dest": "/index.html" }
  ]
}
```

**Modern (rewrites)**: Filesystem check is default behavior
```json
{
  "rewrites": [
    { "source": "/(.*)", "destination": "/index.html" }
  ]
}
```

#### Negative Lookahead
**Legacy (routes)**: Use PCRE Regex negative lookahead directly
```json
{
  "routes": [
    { "src": "/(?!maintenance)", "dest": "/maintenance" }
  ]
}
```

**Modern (rewrites)**: Wrap regex in capture group
```json
{
  "rewrites": [
    { "source": "/((?!maintenance).*)", "destination": "/maintenance" }
  ]
}
```

#### Case Sensitivity
**Legacy (routes)**: Case-insensitive matching (can create duplicate content)
**Modern**: Case-sensitive matching (prevents accidental duplicates)
```

### Python enumerate Function Example

Source: https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html

The enumerate() function returns an enumerate object. It takes an iterable and an optional start value, yielding tuples of count and values from the iterable. This is useful for iterating with an index.

```python
seasons = ['Spring', 'Summer', 'Fall', 'Winter']
print(list(enumerate(seasons)))
# Output: [(0, 'Spring'), (1, 'Summer'), (2, 'Fall'), (3, 'Winter')]

print(list(enumerate(seasons, start=1)))
# Output: [(1, 'Spring'), (2, 'Summer'), (3, 'Fall'), (4, 'Winter')]

def custom_enumerate(iterable, start=0):
    n = start
    for elem in iterable:
        yield n, elem
        n += 1

print(list(custom_enumerate(seasons)))
# Output: [(0, 'Spring'), (1, 'Summer'), (2, 'Fall'), (3, 'Winter')]
```

### Installing Specific Versions and Ranges with npm Install

Source: https://docs.npmjs.com/cli/v8/commands/npm-install

Explains how to install a package by its exact version, a specific tag (like 'latest'), or a version range. Version ranges often require quoting to be treated as a single argument by the shell.

```bash
npm install sax@latest
npm install @myorg/mypackage@latest
npm install sax@0.1.1
npm install @myorg/privatepackage@1.5.0
npm install sax=">=0.1.0 <0.2.0"
npm install @myorg/privatepackage@"16 - 17"
```

### PUT /v1/installations - Upsert Installation

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Create or update a Vercel Marketplace integration installation. This endpoint manages installation configuration and provides access credentials for API authentication.

```APIDOC
## PUT /v1/installations

### Description
Create or update a Vercel Marketplace integration installation. Returns installation details including access credentials for subsequent API calls.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/v1/installations

### Parameters

#### Request Body
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The installation identifier
- **integrationId** (string) - Required - The integration identifier from Vercel Marketplace
- **accountId** (string) - Required - The Vercel account ID
- **credentials** (object) - Required - Authentication credentials including access_token
- **config** (object) - Optional - Installation configuration

### Request Example
```json
{
  "installationId": "icfg_PSFtkFqr5djKRtOkNtOHIfSd",
  "integrationId": "oac_9f4YG9JFjgKkRlxoaaGG0y05",
  "accountId": "acc_1234567890abcdef",
  "credentials": {
    "access_token": "token_example_value"
  },
  "config": {
    "enabled": true
  }
}
```

### Response

#### Success Response (200)
- **installationId** (string) - The installation identifier
- **integrationId** (string) - The integration identifier
- **accountId** (string) - The account identifier
- **credentials** (object) - Contains access_token for API authentication
- **status** (string) - Installation status
- **createdAt** (string) - Creation timestamp
- **updatedAt** (string) - Last update timestamp

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "installationId": "icfg_PSFtkFqr5djKRtOkNtOHIfSd",
  "integrationId": "oac_9f4YG9JFjgKkRlxoaaGG0y05",
  "accountId": "acc_1234567890abcdef",
  "credentials": {
    "access_token": "token_example_value"
  },
  "status": "active",
  "createdAt": "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z",
  "updatedAt": "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z"
}
```
```

### Sanic 'Hello World' Example

Source: https://sanic.readthedocs.io/

A basic 'Hello World' application using the Sanic web framework in Python. It defines a simple route '/' that returns a JSON response. The application can be run using the command 'sanic hello.app'.

```python
from sanic import Sanic
from sanic.response import json

app = Sanic("my-hello-world-app")

@app.route('/')
async def test(request):
    return json({'hello': 'world'})

if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run()
```

### Storefront API Client Example (Ruby SDK)

Source: https://shopify.dev/docs/api/storefront

Shows how to use the ShopifyAPI Ruby gem to interact with the Storefront API.

```APIDOC
## ShopifyAPI Storefront Client (Ruby SDK)

### Description
Uses the ShopifyAPI Ruby gem to create a Storefront client and execute a GraphQL query for products.

### Method
N/A (SDK client method)

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Request Body (for `storefront_client.query`)
- **query** (String) - Required - The GraphQL query string.

### Request Example
```ruby
# Load the access token as per instructions above
storefront_access_token = ''
# Shop from which we're fetching data
shop = 'my-shop.myshopify.com'

# The Storefront client takes in the shop url and the Storefront Access Token for that shop.
storefront_client = ShopifyAPI::Clients::Graphql::Storefront.new(
  shop,
  storefront_access_token
)

# Call query and pass your query as `data`
my_query = <<~QUERY
  {
    products (first: 3) {
      edges {
        node {
          id
          title
        }
      }
    }
  }
QUERY

products = storefront_client.query(query: my_query)
```

### Response
#### Success Response
- **products** (Object) - The result of the GraphQL query, containing product data.

#### Response Example
```ruby
# Assuming products is the parsed JSON response
# products might look like:
# {
#   "data": {
#     "products": {
#       "edges": [
#         {
#           "node": {
#             "id": "gid://shopify/Product/1234567890",
#             "title": "Sample Product 1"
#           }
#         }
#         // ... more products
#       ]
#     }
#   }
# }
```
```

### Child Application Development Configuration

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/microfrontends/configuration

Defines settings for running a child application locally. This includes the local port or host, the task to start the development server, and a fallback URL. The `local` property can be a number (port) or a string (host with optional protocol and port). The `task` should reference a `package.json` script, defaulting to 'dev'. The `fallback` provides a URL for child apps if they don't have their own.

```json
{
  "development": {
    "local": 8080,
    "task": "dev",
    "fallback": "https://example.com:8080"
  }
}
```

### Configure eslint-plugin-eslint-comments in .eslintrc

Source: https://mysticatea.github.io/eslint-plugin-eslint-comments

Configure the ESLint plugin in your .eslintrc file by extending the recommended configuration. Optionally enable the no-unused-disable rule to report unused ESLint disable directives similar to the --report-unused-disable-directives CLI option.

```json
{
  "extends": [
    "eslint:recommended",
    "plugin:eslint-comments/recommended"
  ],
  "rules": {
    "eslint-comments/no-unused-disable": "error"
  }
}
```

### Using Custom Environments via Vercel SDK

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/deployments/local-env

Example of how to create a custom environment using the official Vercel SDK for JavaScript.

```APIDOC
## Using Custom Environments via Vercel SDK

### Description
Programmatically create a custom environment using the `@vercel/sdk` package in your Node.js application.

### Code Example
```javascript
import { Vercel } from '@vercel/sdk';

const vercel = new Vercel({
  bearerToken: 'YOUR_VERCEL_TOKEN',
});

async function createEnvironment() {
  try {
    const result = await vercel.environment.createCustomEnvironment({
      projectId: 'YOUR_PROJECT_ID',
      requestBody: {
        slug: 'qa',
        description: 'Quality Assurance environment',
      },
    });
    console.log('Custom environment created:', result);
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error creating custom environment:', error);
  }
}

createEnvironment();
```
```

### Using semver as a Command-Line Utility

Source: https://github.com/npm/node-semver

This example illustrates how to use the semver package directly from the command line. It shows the basic usage and help command (`semver -h`). It also details various command-line options for filtering versions by range, incrementing versions, handling loose parsing, and including prerelease versions.

```bash
$ semver -h
A JavaScript implementation of the https://semver.org/ specification
Copyright Isaac Z. Schlueter
Usage: semver [options] [[<lev>] <ver>] ...

Options:
  -r, --range          Print versions that match the specified range.
  -i, --increment [level] Increment a version by the specified level. Level can be one of:
                       major, minor, patch, premajor, preminor, prepatch, prerelease, or release.
                       Default level is 'patch'. Only one version may be specified.
  --preid <identifier> Identifier to be used to prefix premajor, preminor, prepatch or prerelease version increments.
  -l, --loose          Interpret versions and ranges loosely
  -n <0|1>             This is the base to be used for the prerelease identifier.
  -p, --include-prerelease Always include prerelease versions in range matching
  -c, --coerce         Coerce a string into SemVer if possible (does not imply --loose)
```

### POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/accept

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Completes the resource transfer process. Expects that all required work to move resources from one installation to another on the provider's side is or will be completed successfully. The installation ID in the URL is the target installation ID, not the source.

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/accept

### Description
Accept Resources Transfer Request - Finish the transfer process. Resources will be moved from source to target installation while maintaining project connection. No other request to complete the same transfer can be processed while transfer is in progress. After completion, transfer cannot be completed again or verified.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}/resource-transfer-requests/{providerClaimId}/accept`

### Security
System Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the target installation to transfer resources to. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"
- **providerClaimId** (string) - Required - The provider-specific claim ID for the resource transfer

### Response
#### Success Response (204)
No content - Transfer completed successfully

#### Response Codes
- 204 - No Content
- 403 - Forbidden
- 404 - Not Found
- 409 - Conflict
- 422 - Unprocessable Entity
```

--------------------------------

### Simula: BASICIO Class for File Handling

Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_streams

Example of a Simula class 'BASICIO' demonstrating object-oriented file handling, including standard input and output streams.

```simula
class BASICIO (LINELENGTH);
integer LINELENGTH;
begin
ref (infile) SYSIN;
ref (infile) procedure sysin;
sysin :- SYSIN;
ref (printfle) SYSOUT;
ref (printfle) procedure sysout;
sysout :- SYSOUT;

class FILE ....................;
FILE class infile ............;
FILE class outfile ...........;
FILE class directfile ........;
outfile class printfle .......;

SYSIN :- new infile ("SYSIN");
SYSOUT :- new printfle ("SYSOUT");

SYSIN.open (blanks(80));
SYSOUT.open(blanks(LINELENGTH));

inner;

SYSIN.close;
SYSOUT.close;
end BASICIO;
```

### Define Route Middleware in Nuxt.js

Source: https://nuxt.com/docs/guide/directory-structure/middleware

Example of defining a named route middleware in Nuxt.js. This middleware checks the route parameters and navigates or aborts based on conditions. It utilizes Nuxt's helper functions for navigation control.

```typescript
export default defineNuxtRouteMiddleware((to, from) => {
  if (to.params.id === '1') {
    return abortNavigation()
  }
  // In a real app you would probably not redirect every route to '/'
  // however it is important to check `to.path` before redirecting or you
  // might get an infinite redirect loop
  if (to.path !== '/') {
    return navigateTo('/')
  }
})
```

### Overview of Building AI Apps on Vercel

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/upgrade-to-zero-configuration

An introductory guide to the key concepts and tools necessary for building and scaling Artificial Intelligence (AI) applications on the Vercel platform. Covers aspects like model deployment, data handling, and leveraging Vercel's infrastructure for AI workloads.

```markdown
# Building AI Apps on Vercel: An Overview

This guide covers the fundamental concepts for developing and deploying AI-powered applications using Vercel.

## Key Concepts

*   **Model Deployment**: Strategies for hosting and serving machine learning models.
*   **Data Processing**: Handling large datasets and real-time data streams.
*   **Scalability**: Leveraging Vercel's serverless architecture for dynamic scaling.
*   **Integration**: Connecting with AI services and APIs.

## Vercel Features for AI

*   **Serverless Functions**: For running inference code and API endpoints.
*   **Edge Functions**: For low-latency AI model execution closer to users.
*   **AI SDK**: Tools and libraries to simplify AI development.
*   **Observability**: Monitoring performance and debugging AI applications.

## Getting Started

1.  **Choose your AI model**: Select or train a suitable machine learning model.
2.  **Containerize or package your model**: Prepare your model for deployment.
3.  **Deploy using Vercel Functions**: Utilize Serverless or Edge Functions.
4.  **Integrate with your frontend**: Connect your AI backend to your user interface.

```

### Storybook Configuration for Button Component

Source: https://vercel.com/templates/react/turborepo-design-system

An example Storybook file for the Button component from `@acme/ui`. It demonstrates how to import the component, use Storybook's addon-docs for documentation (Meta, Story, Preview, Props), and display the component with example content.

```typescript
import { Button } from '@acme/ui/button';
import { Meta, Story, Preview, Props } from '@storybook/addon-docs/blocks';

<Meta title="Components/Button" />

# Button

Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet, consectetur adipiscing elit. Donec euismod, nisl eget consectetur tempor, nisl nunc egestas nisi, euismod aliquam nisl nunc euismod.

## Props

<Props />

## Examples

<Preview>
  <Story name="Primary">
    <Button>Hello</Button>
  </Story>
</Preview>
```

### Get Weather Schema with Additional Properties False (JSON)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs

An example of a 'get_weather' schema where `additionalProperties: false` is explicitly set. This enforces that only the defined 'location' and 'unit' properties are permitted in the schema, aligning with structured output requirements.

```json
{
  "name": "get_weather",
  "description": "Fetches the weather in the given location",
  "strict": true,
  "schema": {
    "type": "object",
    "properties": {
      "location": {
        "type": "string",
        "description": "The location to get the weather for"
      },
      "unit": {
        "type": "string",
        "description": "The unit to return the temperature in",
        "enum": [
          "F",
          "C"
        ]
      }
    },
    "additionalProperties": false,
    "required": [
      "location",
      "unit"
    ]
  }
}
```

### Run Command in Private Git Repo Sandbox (TypeScript)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/vercel-sandbox/examples

This example demonstrates how to create an isolated environment from a private Git repository using the Vercel Sandbox SDK. It authenticates with a GitHub token, sets a timeout, exposes ports, and runs a simple 'echo' command within the sandbox, printing its standard output. The code relies on the '@vercel/sandbox' package and the 'ms' package for timeout configuration.

```typescript
import { Sandbox } from '@vercel/sandbox';
import ms from 'ms';

async function main() {
  const sandbox = await Sandbox.create({
    source: {
      url: 'https://github.com/vercel/some-private-repo.git',
      type: 'git',
      // For GitHub, you can use a fine grained, classic personal access token or GitHub App installation access token
      username: 'x-access-token',
      password: process.env.GIT_ACCESS_TOKEN!,
    },
    timeout: ms('5m'),
    ports: [3000],
  });

  const echo = await sandbox.runCommand('echo', ['Hello sandbox!']);
  console.log(`Message: ${await echo.stdout()}`);
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Delete a Getter Using 'delete' Operator (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example illustrates how to remove a getter property from an object using the `delete` operator. After deletion, accessing the property will result in `undefined`.

```javascript
const obj = {
  get prop() {
    return 'value';
  }
};

console.log(obj.prop); // 'value'
delete obj.prop;
console.log(obj.prop); // undefined
```

### HTTP Request with Signature Headers

Source: https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/draft-meunier-web-bot-auth-architecture

Shows a complete HTTP GET request with signature authentication headers including Signature, Signature-Input, and optional Signature-Agent headers. The example demonstrates the cryptographic material exchange between agent and origin with base64-encoded signature values and timing parameters.

```http
GET /path/to/resource
Signature: abc==
Signature-Input: sig=("@authority" "signature-agent";key="sig");\
created=1700000000;\
expires=1700011111;\
keyid="ba3e64==";\
tag="web-bot-auth"
Signature-Agent: sig="https://signer.example.com"
```

### Module Instantiation and Evaluation Workflow in Node.js VM

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/vm.html

Complete workflow demonstrating module creation, dependency linking, instantiation, and evaluation. Shows how to set up a module context, resolve dependencies recursively, instantiate the module, and then evaluate it to execute the code.

```javascript
// Step 1: Create module with context
const rootModule = new vm.SourceTextModule(`
export default secret;
`, { context: module.context });

const moduleMap = new Map();

// Step 2: Resolve and link dependencies
function resolveAndLinkDependencies(module) {
  const requestedModules = [];
  // Link modules with linker callback
  module.link((specifier) => {
    let requestedModule = moduleMap.get(specifier);
    if (!requestedModule) {
      requestedModule = new vm.SourceTextModule(`
export default secret;
`, { context: module.context });
      moduleMap.set(specifier, requestedModule);
      // Recursively resolve dependencies
      resolveAndLinkDependencies(requestedModule);
    }
    return requestedModule;
  });
  module.linkRequests(requestedModules);
}

resolveAndLinkDependencies(rootModule);
rootModule.instantiate();

// Step 3: Evaluate the module
await rootModule.evaluate();
// Prints 42
```

### Request Upgrade Example

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/http.html

Demonstrates how to set up an HTTP server that handles the 'upgrade' event for WebSocket connections and how a client can request such an upgrade.

```APIDOC
## Example: Handling 'upgrade' Event

```javascript
import http from 'node:http';
import process from 'node:process';

// Create an HTTP server
const server = http.createServer((req, res) => {
  res.writeHead(200, { 'Content-Type': 'text/plain' });
  res.end('okay');
});

server.on('upgrade', (req, socket, head) => {
  socket.write('HTTP/1.1 101 Web Socket Protocol Handshake\r\n' +
               'Upgrade: WebSocket\r\n' +
               'Connection: Upgrade\r\n' +
               '\r\n');
  socket.pipe(socket); // echo back
});

// Now that server is running
server.listen(1337, '127.0.0.1', () => {
  // make a request
  const options = {
    port: 1337,
    host: '127.0.0.1',
    headers: {
      'Connection': 'Upgrade',
      'Upgrade': 'websocket',
    },
  };

  const req = http.request(options);
  req.end();

  req.on('upgrade', (res, socket, upgradeHead) => {
    console.log('got upgraded!');
    socket.end();
    process.exit(0);
  });
});
```
```

### POST /api/chat

API route for handling chat messages and tool invocations.

test('top level test', async (t) => {

### Initialize and Use Computer Tool with Vertex AI Anthropic

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/providers/ai-sdk-providers/google-vertex

Illustrates the setup for the Computer Tool, enabling control over keyboard and mouse actions. The `execute` function defines how to handle various actions like 'key', 'type', 'mouse_move', 'left_click', 'screenshot', etc. It requires parameters such as `action`, `coordinate`, and `text`, depending on the action performed. The `toModelOutput` function is provided to map tool results for LLM consumption.

```typescript
const computerTool = vertexAnthropic.tools.computer_20241022({
  displayWidthPx: 1920,
  displayHeightPx: 1080,
  displayNumber: 0, // Optional, for X11 environments
  execute: async ({ action, coordinate, text }) => {
    // Implement your computer control logic here
    // Return the result of the action
    // Example code:
    switch (action) {
      case 'screenshot': {
        // multipart result: return { type: 'image', data: fs
        //   .readFileSync('./data/screenshot-editor.png')
        //   .toString('base64'),
        // };
      }
      default: {
        console.log('Action:', action);
        console.log('Coordinate:', coordinate);
        console.log('Text:', text);
        return `executed ${action}`;
      }
    }
  },
  // map to tool result content for LLM consumption:
  toModelOutput(result) {
    return typeof result === 'string' ? [{ type: 'text', text: result }]
      : [{ type: 'image', data: result.data, mediaType: 'image/png' }];
  },
});
```

### Installation-level Billing Plans Configuration

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/submit-integration

Optional toggle to enable billing plan selection at the installation level. When enabled, allows users to select and manage billing plans for their installation.

```APIDOC
## Installation-level Billing Plans Configuration

### Description
Optional feature that allows integration users to select a billing plan for their installation. When enabled, provides a default plan that can be customized by users.

### Configuration
- **Required**: No (toggle disabled by default)
- **Applies to**: Installation level

### When to Enable
Enable this toggle if billing for your integration happens at the team, organization, or account level. This allows Vercel to fetch and present installation-level billing plans to users.

### Default Behavior
When enabled, the default installation-level billing plan is chosen by the partner.

### User Capabilities
When enabled, users can:
- Select an installation-level billing plan during setup
- Update the installation-level plan at any time from the installation detail page in the Vercel dashboard

### Partner Responsibilities
When a user selects an installation-level billing plan, you can then upgrade the plan for the associated team, account, or organization during product provisioning.

### Disabled State
When disabled, the installation does not have a configurable billing plan.
```

### Derived Store Example in React

Source: https://vercel.com/templates/starter/tanstack-start-on-vercel

This code snippet demonstrates how to create and use a derived store in a React application using the TanStack Store library. It initializes a store and then creates a derived store that updates based on the initial store. The derived store can then be accessed within a component using the `useStore` hook. This pattern is useful for creating reactive state that depends on other state variables.

```javascript
import { useStore } from '@tanstack/react-store';
import { store, Derived } from './store'; // Assuming 'store' and 'Derived' are exported from './store'

function App() {
  const derivedState = useStore(store, (state) => state.derivedValue);

  return (
    <div>
      <h1>Derived Store Example</h1>
      <p>Derived Value: {derivedState}</p>
    </div>
  );
}

// In './store.js' or similar:
// export const initialStore = new Store({ value: 10 });
// export const derivedStore = new Derived(initialStore, (state) => ({ derivedValue: state.value * 2 }));
// derivedStore.mount(); // Start updates

export default App;
```

### Node.js Lambda Handler Project Setup

Source: https://docs.aws.amazon.com/lambda/latest/dg/nodejs-handler.html

Initialize a Node.js Lambda project using npm and understand the project structure. This sets up the foundation for your Lambda function with proper metadata and dependency management.

```APIDOC
## Project Setup

### Description
Initialize a Node.js Lambda project using npm package manager

### Command
```
npm init
```

### Project Structure
A typical Node.js Lambda function project follows this structure:

```
/project-root
├── index.mjs          — Contains main handler
├── package.json       — Project metadata and dependencies
├── package-lock.json  — Dependency lock file
└── node_modules/      — Installed dependencies
```

### Files
- **index.mjs** - Main handler file (supports both ES module and CommonJS)
- **package.json** - Manages project metadata and dependencies
- **package-lock.json** - Lock file for reproducible dependency installation
- **node_modules/** - Directory containing installed npm packages

### Handler File Format
Function code lives in a `.js` or `.mjs` JavaScript file. Use `.mjs` for ES module handlers and `.js` for CommonJS handlers.
```

### FastAPI Application Example for Vercel

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/frameworks/backend/fastapi

A minimal FastAPI application example. It includes a root endpoint and a handler for favicon.ico, which is automatically served if placed in the public directory. Note that `app.mount('/public', ...)` is not needed.

```python
from fastapi import FastAPI
from fastapi.responses import RedirectResponse

app = FastAPI()

@app.get("/favicon.ico", include_in_schema=False)
async def favicon():
    # /vercel.svg is automatically served when included in the public/** directory.
    return RedirectResponse("/vercel.svg", status_code=307)
```

### Read 'x-vercel-id' Header in Vercel Functions

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/headers/request-headers

This example demonstrates how to get the 'x-vercel-id' header, which provides information about the Vercel regions the request traversed and the execution region of the function. This header is also used by Vercel to prevent infinite request loops.

```typescript
export function GET(request: Request) {
  const vercelId = request.headers.get('x-vercel-id');
  return new Response(`Vercel ID: ${vercelId}`);
}
```

### Get Active Attack Status using Vercel SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/sdk/blob/HEAD/docs/sdks/security/README

Retrieves the active attack status for a given project. This example demonstrates using the Vercel SDK, requiring a bearer token and project/team identifiers. It handles successful responses and errors.

```typescript
import { VercelCore } from "@vercel/sdk/core.js";
import { securityGetActiveAttackStatus } from "@vercel/sdk/funcs/securityGetActiveAttackStatus.js";

const vercel = new VercelCore({
  bearerToken: "<YOUR_BEARER_TOKEN_HERE>",
});

async function run() {
  const res = await securityGetActiveAttackStatus(vercel, {
    projectId: "<id>",
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug",
  });
  if (res.ok) {
    const { value: result } = res;
    console.log(result);
  } else {
    console.log("securityGetActiveAttackStatus failed:", res.error);
  }
}

run();
```

### Create Chat API Route Handler

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nuxt

Define a server-side API route that handles chat requests, initializes the OpenAI provider, processes incoming messages, and returns streamed text responses. This route acts as the backend for the AI chatbot functionality.

```typescript
import { streamText, UIMessage, convertToModelMessages } from 'ai';
import { createOpenAI } from '@ai-sdk/openai';

export default defineLazyEventHandler(async () => {
  const apiKey = useRuntimeConfig().openaiApiKey;
  if (!apiKey) throw new Error('Missing OpenAI API key');

  const openai = createOpenAI({
    apiKey: apiKey,
  });

  return defineEventHandler(async (event: any) => {
    const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await readBody(event);
    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    });
    return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
  });
});
```

### Invalid export target paths in package.json

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/packages.html

Shows common invalid patterns for export targets that violate Node.js path rules. Examples include absolute paths, file:// URLs, and relative paths that start without './', all of which are rejected for security and encapsulation reasons.

```json
{
  "name": "my-package",
  "exports": {
    "./origin-relative": "/dist/main.js",
    "./absolute": "file:///dev/null",
    "./outside": "../common/util.js"
  }
}
```

### Prepare Command for Cross-Platform Execution (Windows Focus)

Source: https://github.com/yarnpkg/berry/issues/5831

This comprehensive function prepares a command for execution, with a strong focus on Windows compatibility. It first resolves the command's full path, then checks for and interprets shebangs (`wfe`). For Windows, it applies argument escaping (`nU.command`, `nU.argument`) and wraps the entire command in `cmd.exe /d /s /c "..."` to handle complex arguments and pathing, especially for `.cmd` files in `node_modules/.bin`.

```javascript
var Cfe=J("path"),
  iU=VK(),
  nU=XK(),
  mfe=rU(),
  Efe=process.platform==="win32",
  Ife=/\\.(?:com|exe)$/i,
  yfe=/node_modules[\\\/].bin[\\\/][^\\\/]+\\.cmd$/i;
function wfe(r){
  r.file=iU(r);
  let e=r.file&&mfe(r.file);
  return e?(r.args.unshift(r.file),r.command=e,iU(r)):r.file;
}
function Bfe(r){
  if(!Efe)return r;
  let e=wfe(r),
    t=!Ife.test(e);
  if(r.options.forceShell||t){
    let i=yfe.test(e);
    r.command=Cfe.normalize(r.command);
    r.command=nU.command(r.command);
    r.args=r.args.map(s=>nU.argument(s,i));
    let n=[r.command].concat(r.args).join(" ");
    r.args=["/d","/s","/c",`"${n}"`];
    r.command=process.env.comspec||"cmd.exe";
    r.options.windowsVerbatimArguments=!0;
  }
  return r;
}
function bfe(r,e,t){
  e&&!Array.isArray(e)&&(t=e,e=null);
}
```

### project.rolling-release.started

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/webhooks/webhooks-api

This event occurs whenever a rolling release is started. It includes details about the project, the team, the user, and the configuration of the newly started rolling release.

```APIDOC
## Event: project.rolling-release.started

### Description
Occurs whenever a rolling release is started. This event provides details about the project, team, user, and the initial configuration of the rolling release, including deployment IDs, state, and target environment.

### Method
N/A (Webhook Event)

### Endpoint
N/A (Webhook Event)

### Parameters
#### Payload Fields
- **payload.team.id** (ID) - The ID of the event's team (possibly null).
- **payload.user.id** (ID) - The ID of the event's user.
- **payload.project.id** (ID) - The ID of the project.
- **payload.project.name** (String) - Name of the project.
- **payload.rollingRelease** (Object) - The started rolling release configuration.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.projectId** (ID) - The ID of the project.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.ownerId** (ID) - The ID of the team or user that owns the rolling release.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.deploymentIds** (List) - Array of deployment IDs involved in the rolling release.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.state** (String) - The state of the rolling release (will be `ACTIVE`).
  - **payload.rollingRelease.activeStageIndex** (Number) - The index of the initial stage (usually 0).
  - **payload.rollingRelease.default** (Object) - The initial deployment configuration.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.default.baseDeploymentId** (ID) - The ID of the base deployment.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.default.targetDeploymentId** (ID) - The ID of the target deployment.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.default.targetPercentage** (Number) - The initial target percentage for the first stage.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.default.targetStartAt** (Number) - The timestamp when the rolling release started.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.default.targetUpdatedAt** (Number) - The timestamp when the rolling release was last updated.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.config** (Object) - The rolling release configuration.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.config.target** (String) - The target environment for the rolling release.
    - **payload.rollingRelease.config.stages** (List) - Array of stage configurations.
  - **payload.rollingRelease.writtenBy** (String) - The source that started the rolling release.
- **payload.prevRollingRelease** (Object) - The previous rolling release configuration (if any) before starting the new one.
```

### Curl Request with JSON Schema for Math Tutor

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs

This example demonstrates how to make a curl request to an API endpoint to get structured output from a math tutor model. It includes the system and user prompts, and specifies the JSON schema for the response.

```bash
curl https://api.openai.com/v1/responses \
 -H "Authorization: Bearer $OPENAI_API_KEY" \
 -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
 -d '{
   "model": "gpt-4o-2024-08-06",
   "input": [
     { "role": "system", "content": "You are a helpful math tutor. Guide the user through the solution step by step." },
     { "role": "user", "content": "how can I solve 8x + 7 = -23" }
   ],
   "text": {
     "format": {
       "type": "json_schema",
       "name": "math_response",
       "schema": {
         "type": "object",
         "properties": {
           "steps": {
             "type": "array",
             "items": {
               "type": "object",
               "properties": {
                 "explanation": {"type": "string"},
                 "output": {"type": "string"}
               },
               "required": ["explanation", "output"],
               "additionalProperties": false
             }
           },
           "final_answer": {"type": "string"}
         },
         "required": ["steps", "final_answer"],
         "additionalProperties": false
       },
       "strict": true
     }
   }
 }'
```

### Get Bypass IP List using Vercel SDK

Source: https://github.com/vercel/sdk/blob/HEAD/docs/sdks/security/README

Retrieves system bypass rules configured for a specific project. This example shows how to use the Vercel SDK with a bearer token, project, and team details. It logs the result or any errors encountered.

```typescript
import { Vercel } from "@vercel/sdk";

const vercel = new Vercel({
  bearerToken: "<YOUR_BEARER_TOKEN_HERE>",
});

async function run() {
  const result = await vercel.security.getBypassIp({
    projectId: "<id>",
    limit: 10,
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug",
  });

  console.log(result);
}

run();
```

```typescript
import { VercelCore } from "@vercel/sdk/core.js";
import { securityGetBypassIp } from "@vercel/sdk/funcs/securityGetBypassIp.js";

const vercel = new VercelCore({
  bearerToken: "<YOUR_BEARER_TOKEN_HERE>",
});

async function run() {
  const res = await securityGetBypassIp(vercel, {
    projectId: "<id>",
    limit: 10,
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug",
  });
  if (res.ok) {
    const { value: result } = res;
    console.log(result);
  } else {
    console.log("securityGetBypassIp failed:", res.error);
  }
}

run();
```

  // ... other options
  onStepFinish({
    text,
    toolCalls,
    toolResults,
    finishReason,
    usage,
  }) {
    // Your own logic, e.g. for saving the chat history or recording usage
    console.log('Step finished:', { text, toolCalls, toolResults, finishReason, usage });
  },
});

### Use a Computed Property Name for Getter (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example shows how to use an expression for a computed property name to define a getter. The property name is dynamically determined by the value of the `propertyName` variable.

```javascript
const propertyName = 'dynamicProp';
const obj = {
  get [propertyName]() {
    return 'computed value';
  }
};

console.log(obj.dynamicProp); // 'computed value'
```

### Pagination Example - Node.js Implementation

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/rest-api/reference

Complete example demonstrating how to iterate through paginated API responses using Node.js and axios, fetching all projects and saving them to a JSON file.

```APIDOC
## GET /v9/projects - Fetch All Projects with Pagination

### Description
Retrieve all projects from a Vercel account using pagination to handle large result sets.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
https://api.vercel.com/v9/projects

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **limit** (integer) - Optional - Items per page (default: 20, max: 100)
- **until** (timestamp) - Optional - Pagination cursor from previous response

### Request Example (Node.js)
```javascript
const axios = require('axios');
const fs = require('fs');
const vercelToken = 'yourtokenvalue';
const apiEndPt = 'https://api.vercel.com/v9/projects';

let config = {
  method: 'get',
  url: apiEndPt,
  headers: {
    Authorization: 'Bearer ' + vercelToken
  }
};

let results = [];

(function loop() {
  axios(config)
    .then(function (response) {
      results.push(...response.data.projects);
      if (response.data.pagination.next !== null) {
        config.url = `${apiEndPt}?until=${response.data.pagination.next}`;
        loop();
      } else {
        fs.writeFileSync('projects.json', JSON.stringify(results));
      }
    })
    .catch(function (error) {
      console.log(error);
    });
})();
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **projects** (array) - Array of project objects
- **pagination** (object) - Pagination metadata object
```

### Express App with Port Listener

Source: https://vercel.com/guides/using-express-with-vercel

This Express.js application example demonstrates how to use `app.listen` to expose the server on a specific port. This pattern is useful for running the application locally or in environments where direct port access is managed. It includes a root route and a callback for when the server starts.

```typescript
// Use "type: module" in package.json to use ES modules
import express from 'express';
const app = express();
const port = 3000;

// Define your routes
app.get('/', (req, res) => {
  res.json({ message: 'Hello from Express on Vercel!' });
});

app.listen(port, () => {

});

### Redact Sensitive Information in Astro Middleware

Source: https://docs.astro.build/en/guides/middleware

This middleware intercepts responses, reads the HTML content, and replaces all occurrences of 'PRIVATE INFO' with 'REDACTED'. It's useful for removing sensitive data before rendering the final HTML. This example assumes a basic Astro setup.

```javascript
export const onRequest = async (context, next) => {
  const response = await next();
  const html = await response.text();
  const redactedHtml = html.replaceAll("PRIVATE INFO", "REDACTED");
  return new Response(redactedHtml, { status: 200, headers: response.headers });
};
```

### Fortran 77 Example for Standard Input/Output

Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_streams

Demonstrates reading an integer from standard input (UNIT=5) and writing it to standard output (UNIT=6) using Fortran 77 conventions.

```fortran
! FORTRAN 77 example
PROGRAM MAIN
INTEGER NUMBER
READ(UNIT=5,*) NUMBER
WRITE(UNIT=6,'(A,I3)') ' NUMBER IS: ',NUMBER
END
```

### Stream Text with Groq and Vercel AI SDK

Source: https://vercel.com/marketplace/groq

Demonstrates streaming text generation using the Vercel AI SDK with Groq's llama-3.3-70b-versatile model. The example imports necessary functions, initializes a streaming request with a prompt, and outputs the response chunks to the console in real-time. Requires GROQ_API_KEY environment variable to be set.

```javascript
import { streamText } from 'ai';
import { groq } from '@ai-sdk/groq';

async function main() {
  const result = streamText({
    model: groq('llama-3.3-70b-versatile'),
    prompt: 'Why do Vercel and Groq work so well together?'
  });

  for await (const textPart of result.textStream) {
    process.stdout.write(textPart);
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Omit Dependencies during Installation

Source: https://bun.sh/docs/cli/install

The `--omit` flag allows you to exclude specific types of dependencies (e.g., `dev`, `peer`, `optional`) during `bun install`. This provides fine-grained control over which dependencies are included in your project, especially useful for optimizing install sizes.

```bash
# Exclude "devDependencies" from the installation.
bun install --omit dev

# Install only dependencies from "dependencies"
bun install --omit=dev --omit=peer --omit=optional
```

### Trace Async Resource Initialization with triggerAsyncId in Node.js

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/async_hooks.html

This example demonstrates how to use Node.js's 'async_hooks' to track asynchronous resource initialization. It logs the resource type, its ID, the ID of the resource that triggered it ('triggerAsyncId'), and the current execution context ('executionAsyncId'). It then starts a TCP server to observe the output.

```javascript
import { createHook, executionAsyncId } from 'node:async_hooks';
import { stdout } from 'node:process';
import net from 'node:net';
import fs from 'node:fs';

createHook({
  init(asyncId, type, triggerAsyncId) {
    const eid = executionAsyncId();
    fs.writeSync(stdout.fd, `${type}(${asyncId}): trigger: ${triggerAsyncId} execution: ${eid}\n`);
  },
}).enable();

net.createServer((conn) => {}).listen(8080);

// Equivalent CommonJS version:
const { createHook, executionAsyncId } = require('node:async_hooks');
const { stdout } = require('node:process');
const net = require('node:net');
const fs = require('node:fs');

createHook({
  init(asyncId, type, triggerAsyncId) {
    const eid = executionAsyncId();
    fs.writeSync(stdout.fd, `${type}(${asyncId}): trigger: ${triggerAsyncId} execution: ${eid}\n`);
  },
}).enable();

net.createServer((conn) => {}).listen(8080);
```

### Function Tool Example (Python)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/function-calling

An end-to-end tool calling flow example for a `get_horoscope` function using Python.

```APIDOC
## Function Tool Example (Python)

Let's look at an end-to-end tool calling flow for a `get_horoscope` function that gets a daily horoscope for an astrological sign.

### Method
`POST`

### Endpoint
`/v1/chat/completions` (Implicitly used by `client.responses.create`)

### Parameters

#### Request Body (Conceptual for `client.responses.create`)

- **model** (string) - Required - The model to use (e.g., "gpt-5").
- **tools** (array) - Required - A list of tool definitions the model can use.
- **input** (array) - Required - The conversation history and tool outputs.
- **instructions** (string) - Optional - Instructions for the model's final response.

#### Tool Definition (`tools` parameter)

- **type** (string) - Required - Must be `"function"`.
- **name** (string) - Required - The name of the function (e.g., `"get_horoscope"`).
- **description** (string) - Optional - Details on when and how to use the function.
- **parameters** (object) - Required - JSON schema defining the function's input arguments.
  - **type** (string) - Required - Must be `"object"`.
  - **properties** (object) - Required - Defines the properties (arguments) the function accepts.
    - **sign** (string) - Required - Description of the `sign` parameter (e.g., "An astrological sign like Taurus or Aquarius").
  - **required** (array) - Required - List of required parameter names (e.g., `["sign"]`).

### Request Example (Python Code Snippet)

```python
from openai import OpenAI
import json

client = OpenAI()

# 1. Define a list of callable tools for the model
tools = [
  {
    "type": "function",
    "name": "get_horoscope",
    "description": "Get today's horoscope for an astrological sign.",
    "parameters": {
      "type": "object",
      "properties": {
        "sign": {
          "type": "string",
          "description": "An astrological sign like Taurus or Aquarius",
        },
      },
      "required": ["sign"],
    },
  },
]

def get_horoscope(sign):
    return f"{sign}: Next Tuesday you will befriend a baby otter."

# Create a running input list we will add to over time
input_list = [
    {"role": "user", "content": "What is my horoscope? I am an Aquarius."}
]

# 2. Prompt the model with tools defined
response = client.responses.create(
    model="gpt-5",
    tools=tools,
    input=input_list,
)

# Save function call outputs for subsequent requests
input_list += response.output

for item in response.output:
    if item.type == "function_call":
        if item.name == "get_horoscope":
            # 3. Execute the function logic for get_horoscope
            horoscope = get_horoscope(json.loads(item.arguments))
            # 4. Provide function call results to the model
            input_list.append({
                "type": "function_call_output",
                "call_id": item.call_id,
                "output": json.dumps({"horoscope": horoscope})
            })

print("Final input:")
print(input_list)

response = client.responses.create(
    model="gpt-5",
    instructions="Respond only with a horoscope generated by a tool.",
    tools=tools,
    input=input_list,
)

# 5. The model should be able to give a response!
print("Final output:")
print(response.model_dump_json(indent=2))
print("\n" + response.output_text)
```
```

```APIDOC
## POST /v1/responses

### Description
This endpoint allows you to generate text responses from OpenAI models. You can specify the desired model and provide an input prompt to receive a generated output.

### Endpoint

### Parameters

### Node.js: Create Streaming AI Chatbot

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nodejs

This Node.js code implements a command-line chatbot using the AI SDK. It sets up terminal input/output, maintains conversation history in a messages array, and uses streamText with the OpenAI provider to generate and stream responses from the AI model. User input is captured, sent to the model, and the assistant's response is displayed incrementally.

```typescript
import { openai } from '@ai-sdk/openai';
import { ModelMessage, streamText } from 'ai';
import 'dotenv/config';
import * as readline from 'node:readline/promises';

const terminal = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
});

const messages: ModelMessage[] = [];

async function main() {
  while (true) {
    const userInput = await terminal.question('You: ');
    messages.push({ role: 'user', content: userInput });

    const result = streamText({
      model: openai('gpt-4o'),
      messages,
    });

    let fullResponse = '';
    process.stdout.write('\nAssistant: ');
    for await (const delta of result.textStream) {
      fullResponse += delta;
      process.stdout.write(delta);
    }
    process.stdout.write('\n\n');
    messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content: fullResponse });
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);
```

### Serving Static Files with Hono Node.js

```typescript
import { serveStatic } from '@hono/node-server/serve-static'

// Serve files under ./static for requests to /static/*
app.use('/static/*', serveStatic({ root: './' }))

// Serve favicon.ico from the root directory
app.use('/favicon.ico', serveStatic({ path: './favicon.ico' }))

// Serve files from ./static for requests to /hello.txt or /image.png
app.use('*', serveStatic({ root: './static' }))

### Get Firewall Configuration using Standalone Function

Source: https://github.com/vercel/sdk/blob/HEAD/docs/sdks/security/README

This example demonstrates retrieving Vercel firewall configuration details using a standalone function. It utilizes `VercelCore` for optimized imports and includes checks for successful retrieval of the configuration. The function fetches the active firewall configuration.

```typescript
import { VercelCore } from "@vercel/sdk/core.js";
import { securityGetFirewallConfig } from "@vercel/sdk/funcs/securityGetFirewallConfig.js";

const vercel = new VercelCore({
  bearerToken: "<YOUR_BEARER_TOKEN_HERE>",
});

async function run() {
  const res = await securityGetFirewallConfig(vercel, {
    projectId: "<id>",
    teamId: "team_1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l",
    slug: "my-team-url-slug",
    configVersion: "<value>",
  });
  if (res.ok) {
    const { value: result } = res;
    console.log(result);
  } else {
    console.log("securityGetFirewallConfig failed:", res.error);
  }
}

run();
```

### Express Multiple Route Handlers for a Path (JavaScript)

Source: https://expressjs.com/en/guide/using-middleware.html

This example shows defining two GET handlers for '/user/:id'. The first handler logs the ID and calls next(), while the second sends 'User Info'. The second handler is unreachable because the first one does not end the cycle.

```javascript
app.get('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  console.log('ID:', req.params.id)
  next()
}, (req, res, next) => {
  res.send('User Info')
})

// handler for the /user/:id path, which prints the user ID
app.get('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  res.send(req.params.id)
})
```

### Define Getter on Existing Objects using Object.defineProperty (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example demonstrates how to add a getter to an existing object using the `Object.defineProperty()` method. It defines a getter for the `size` property that returns the length of the `collection` array.

```javascript
const obj = {};
const collection = [1, 2, 3];

Object.defineProperty(obj, 'size', {
  get: function() { return collection.length; },
  enumerable: true,
  configurable: true
});

console.log(obj.size); // 3
```
