### Define Feature Flags in Next.js (flags.ts)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/feature-flags/flags-explorer/getting-started

Defines feature flags within your Next.js project. This file should be located at the root of your project and exports your feature flags. It uses the `flag` function from the 'flags/next' package. The `decide` function determines the flag's boolean value.

```typescript
import { flag } from 'flags/next';

export const exampleFlag = flag({
  key: 'example-flag',
  description: 'An example feature flag',
  decide() {
    return false;
  },
});
```

### robots.txt Examples for Quantcast Bot

Source: https://www.quantcast.com/bot

Examples of robots.txt file configurations to manage access for the Quantcast Bot. These examples demonstrate how to disallow or allow crawling for the Quantcastbot specifically, or for all bots, affecting website accessibility for the crawler.

```robots.txt
# Disallowing crawling of the entire website for all bots:
User-agent: *
Disallow: /

# Disallowing crawling of the entire website for only the Quantcastbot:
User-agent: *
Allow: /
User-agent: Quantcastbot
Disallow: /

# Allow access to all crawlers:
User-agent: *
Allow: /

# Allow access to only Quantcastbot
User-agent: *
Disallow: /
User-agent: Quantcastbot
Allow: /

# Disallow crawling of specific directories and websites in those
```

### nvm Manual Installation

Source: https://github.com/nvm-sh/nvm

Performs a fully manual installation of nvm. It clones the repository, checks out the latest tag, and sources the nvm script, followed by adding configuration to shell profile files.

```shell
export NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm" && \
( git clone https://github.com/nvm-sh/nvm.git "$NVM_DIR"
  cd "$NVM_DIR"
  git checkout `git describe --abbrev=0 --tags --match "v[0-9]*" $(git rev-list --tags --max-count=1)` )
&& \. "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh"
```

### Function Tool Example (JavaScript)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/function-calling

An end-to-end tool calling flow example for a `get_horoscope` function using JavaScript.

```APIDOC
## Function Tool Example (JavaScript)

Let's look at an end-to-end tool calling flow for a `get_horoscope` function that gets a daily horoscope for an astrological sign.

### Method
`POST`

### Endpoint
`/v1/chat/completions` (Implicitly used by `openai.responses.create`)

### Parameters

#### Request Body (Conceptual for `openai.responses.create`)

- **model** (string) - Required - The model to use (e.g., "gpt-5").
- **tools** (array) - Required - A list of tool definitions the model can use.
- **input** (array) - Required - The conversation history and tool outputs.
- **instructions** (string) - Optional - Instructions for the model's final response.

#### Tool Definition (`tools` parameter)

- **type** (string) - Required - Must be `"function"`.
- **name** (string) - Required - The name of the function (e.g., `"get_horoscope"`).
- **description** (string) - Optional - Details on when and how to use the function.
- **parameters** (object) - Required - JSON schema defining the function's input arguments.
  - **type** (string) - Required - Must be `"object"`.
  - **properties** (object) - Required - Defines the properties (arguments) the function accepts.
    - **sign** (string) - Required - Description of the `sign` parameter (e.g., "An astrological sign like Taurus or Aquarius").
  - **required** (array) - Required - List of required parameter names (e.g., `["sign"]`).

### Request Example (JavaScript Code Snippet)

```javascript
import OpenAI from "openai";

const openai = new OpenAI();

// 1. Define a list of callable tools for the model
const tools = [
  {
    type: "function",
    name: "get_horoscope",
    description: "Get today's horoscope for an astrological sign.",
    parameters: {
      type: "object",
      properties: {
        sign: {
          type: "string",
          description: "An astrological sign like Taurus or Aquarius",
        },
      },
      required: ["sign"],
    },
  },
];

function getHoroscope(sign) {
  return sign + " Next Tuesday you will befriend a baby otter.";
}

// Create a running input list we will add to over time
let input = [
  { role: "user", content: "What is my horoscope? I am an Aquarius." },
];

// 2. Prompt the model with tools defined
let response = await openai.responses.create({
  model: "gpt-5",
  tools,
  input,
});

response.output.forEach((item) => {
  if (item.type == "function_call") {
    if (item.name == "get_horoscope") {
      // 3. Execute the function logic for get_horoscope
      const horoscope = getHoroscope(JSON.parse(item.arguments));
      // 4. Provide function call results to the model
      input.push({
        type: "function_call_output",
        call_id: item.call_id,
        output: JSON.stringify({ horoscope }),
      });
    }
  }
});

console.log("Final input:");
console.log(JSON.stringify(input, null, 2));

response = await openai.responses.create({
  model: "gpt-5",
  instructions: "Respond only with a horoscope generated by a tool.",
  tools,
  input,
});

// 5. The model should be able to give a response!
console.log("Final output:");
console.log(JSON.stringify(response.output, null, 2));
```
```

### Manage Cookies in Astro On-Demand Rendering

Source: https://docs.astro.build/en/core-concepts/rendering-modes

This example demonstrates how to check, get, set, and update cookies within an Astro page rendered on demand. It retrieves the current 'counter' cookie, increments its value, and then sets the updated value. This functionality is available at the page level.

```astro
--- 
export const prerender = false; // Not needed in 'server' mode
let counter = 0
if (Astro.cookies.has('counter')) {
  const cookie = Astro.cookies.get('counter')
  const value = cookie?.number()
  if (value !== undefined && !isNaN(value)) counter = value + 1
}
Astro.cookies.set('counter', String(counter))
---

Counter = {counter}
===================

```

### Fetch Data using useQuery in React

Source: https://vercel.com/templates/starter/tanstack-start-on-vercel

Demonstrates how to use the `useQuery` hook from React Query to fetch data from an API. It includes query key definition, data fetching function, and initial data handling.

```typescript
import { useQuery } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import "./App.css";

function App() {
  const { data } = useQuery({
    queryKey: ["people"],
    queryFn: () =>
      fetch("https://swapi.dev/api/people")
        .then((res) => res.json())
        .then((data) => data.results as { name: string }[]),
    initialData: [],
  });

  return (
    <div>
      {data.map((person) => (
        <div key={person.name}>{person.name}</div>
      ))}
    </div>
  );
}

export default App;
```

    "id": "CHALLENGE_COOKIELESS_REQUESTS",

      "type": "CHALLENGE"
    },
    "matches": [

### Skip Middleware on Server or Client in Nuxt

Source: https://nuxt.com/docs/guide/directory-structure/middleware

Define conditional middleware execution using import.meta.server and import.meta.client flags. This example demonstrates how to skip middleware execution in specific environments or during hydration, useful when middleware requires specific browser APIs or when you need to avoid duplicate processing.

```typescript
export default defineNuxtRouteMiddleware((to) => {
  // skip middleware on server
  if (import.meta.server) {
    return
  }
  // skip middleware on client side entirely
  if (import.meta.client) {
    return
  }
  // or only skip middleware on initial client load
  const nuxtApp = useNuxtApp()
  if (import.meta.client && nuxtApp.isHydrating && nuxtApp.payload.serverRendered) {
    return
  }
})
```

### Cache Key Generation Example

Source: https://nitro.unjs.io/guide/cache

Provides an example of how a cache key is generated for a cached function in Nitro. It demonstrates the pattern used, combining group, name, and a generated key. This example shows a function `getAccessToken` with specific options for naming and key generation.

```javascript
const getAccessToken = defineCachedFunction(() => {
  return String(Date.now())
}, {
  maxAge: 10,
  name: 'getAccessToken',
  getKey: () => 'default'
})

// Generated cache key pattern:
nitro:functions:getAccessToken:default.json
```

### Run Tests with TAP Reporter in Node.js

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/test.html

Executes tests defined in files and pipes the output to stdout using the TAP reporter. It configures the test runner to exit with a non-zero code on test failure. This example demonstrates basic test execution and reporting setup.

```javascript
import { tap } from 'node:test/reporters';
import { run } from 'node:test';
import process from 'node:process';
import path from 'node:path';

run({
  files: [path.resolve('./tests/test.js')]
})
  .on('test:fail', () => {
    process.exitCode = 1;
  })
  .compose(tap)
  .pipe(process.stdout);
```

```javascript
const { tap } = require('node:test/reporters');
const { run } = require('node:test');
const path = require('node:path');

run({
  files: [path.resolve('./tests/test.js')]
})
  .on('test:fail', () => {
    process.exitCode = 1;
  })
  .compose(tap)
  .pipe(process.stdout);
```

### Define Static Getters in Classes (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example demonstrates defining a static getter within a JavaScript class. Static getters are called on the class itself, not on instances, and are useful for providing access to static properties or computed static values.

```javascript
class MyClass {
  static get version() {
    return '1.0.0';
  }
}

console.log(MyClass.version); // '1.0.0'

### POST /responses (Structured Outputs - Chain of Thought Example - Python)

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs

Python example demonstrating Structured Outputs for math tutoring, using Pydantic models to define the expected output structure for step-by-step problem-solving.

```APIDOC
## POST /responses (Chain of Thought - Python)

### Description
This Python example utilizes Structured Outputs with Pydantic models to generate a structured, step-by-step solution for a math problem, ensuring adherence to the defined schema.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/v1/responses`

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **model** (string) - Required - The model to use for generation (e.g., `gpt-4o-2024-08-06`).
- **input** (list) - Required - A list of message dictionaries, including system and user prompts.
  - **role** (string) - Required - The role of the message (e.g., `system`, `user`).
  - **content** (string) - Required - The content of the message.
- **text_format** (BaseModel) - Required - A Pydantic model defining the expected output structure.

### Request Example
```python
from openai import OpenAI
from pydantic import BaseModel

client = OpenAI()

class Step(BaseModel):
    explanation: str
    output: str

class MathReasoning(BaseModel):
    steps: list[Step]
    final_answer: str

response = client.responses.parse(
    model="gpt-4o-2024-08-06",
    input=[
        {
            "role": "system",
            "content": "You are a helpful math tutor. Guide the user through the solution step by step."
        },
        {"role": "user", "content": "how can I solve 8x + 7 = -23"},
    ],
    text_format=MathReasoning
)

math_reasoning = response.output_parsed
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **output_parsed** (MathReasoning) - An instance of the `MathReasoning` Pydantic model containing the structured output.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "steps": [
    {
      "explanation": "Start with the equation 8x + 7 = -23.",
      "output": "8x + 7 = -23"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Subtract 7 from both sides to isolate the term with the variable.",
      "output": "8x = -23 - 7"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Simplify the right side of the equation.",
      "output": "8x = -30"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Divide both sides by 8 to solve for x.",
      "output": "x = -30 / 8"
    },
    {
      "explanation": "Simplify the fraction.",
      "output": "x = -15 / 4"
    }
  ],
  "final_answer": "x = -15 / 4"
}
```
```

  children
}: {
  children: ReactNode;

### Client-Side Chat Hook (`useChat`)

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

The `useChat` hook from `@ai-sdk/react` provides client-side state and functions for managing chat interactions.

```APIDOC
## useChat Hook

### Description
Provides client-side state and utility functions for managing chat messages, user input, and sending messages to the chat API.

### Usage
```javascript
'use client';

import { useChat } from '@ai-sdk/react';

function ChatComponent() {
  const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();
  // ... component logic ...
}
```

### State Variables and Functions
- **messages** (array): The current chat messages. Each message is an object with `id`, `role` (e.g., 'user', 'assistant', 'tool'), and `parts` (an array of content parts).
- **sendMessage** (function): A function to send a user message to the chat API. It takes the message text as an argument.
```

### Sequential Data Fetching (Conceptual)

Source: https://nextjs.org/docs/app/building-your-application/data-fetching/fetching-caching-and-revalidating

This snippet illustrates a scenario where data fetching is sequential, meaning one request must complete before the next can start. For example, fetching albums is blocked until the artist data is resolved. This is contrasted with parallel fetching where requests can happen concurrently.

```TypeScript
import { getArtist, getAlbums } from '@/app/lib/data'

export default async function Page({ params }) {
  // These requests will be sequential
  const { username } = await params
  const artist = await getArtist(username)
  const albums = await getAlbums(username)

  return (
    <>
      <h1>{artist.name}</h1>
      {/* Render albums */}
    </>
  )
}
```

### Set Cache Control Headers for Functions (Next.js)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Learn how to set Cache-Control headers for responses generated by your Next.js API routes or serverless functions. Proper caching improves performance and reduces server load. This example shows setting headers in an API route.

```typescript
import type { NextApiRequest, NextApiResponse } from 'next';

export default async function handler(req: NextApiRequest, res: NextApiResponse) {
  // Set Cache-Control header
  // 'public' allows caching by intermediate proxies (CDN, etc.)
  // 'max-age' specifies cache duration in seconds (e.g., 1 hour = 3600 seconds)
  // 'stale-while-revalidate' allows serving stale content while revalidating in the background
  res.setHeader('Cache-Control', 'public, max-age=3600, stale-while-revalidate=86400');

  // Your API logic here
  res.status(200).json({ message: 'Data with caching headers' });
}
```

### Customizing HTTP Client Behavior (Go)

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Shows how to create and configure an HTTP client in Go for more control over request behavior, such as redirect policies. It also illustrates creating custom requests and adding headers.

```Go
client := &http.Client{
    CheckRedirect: redirectPolicyFunc,
}
resp, err := client.Get("http://example.com")
// ...

req, err := http.NewRequest("GET", "http://example.com", nil)
// ...
req.Header.Add("If-None-Match", `W/"wyzzy"`)
resp, err := client.Do(req)
// ...
```

### Modify Request Headers in Middleware (Next.js)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Learn how to modify incoming request headers within your Next.js Middleware. This is useful for adding security headers, forwarding information from the client, or altering headers before they reach the application logic. The example shows adding a custom header.

```typescript
import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'
import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'

export function middleware(request: NextRequest) {
  const requestHeaders = new Headers(request.headers)
  requestHeaders.set('X-Custom-Request-Header', 'Value-From-Middleware')

  // You can also modify existing headers, e.g.:
  // if (requestHeaders.has('User-Agent')) {
  //   requestHeaders.set('User-Agent', 'Modified-By-Middleware')
  // }

  return NextResponse.next({
    request: {
      headers: requestHeaders,
    },
  })
}
```

### Reproducible Installs with --frozen-lockfile

Source: https://bun.sh/docs/cli/install

The `--frozen-lockfile` flag ensures reproducible installations by using the exact package versions specified in `bun.lock`. If `package.json` and `bun.lock` are out of sync, Bun will exit with an error, and the lockfile will not be updated. This prevents unexpected changes during installs.

```bash
bun install --frozen-lockfile
```

### HTTP Client GET Request in Go

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Demonstrates making an HTTP GET request using the `Client.Get` method. This is a convenient way to fetch resources from a URL. The method returns an `http.Response` and an error.

```go
func (c *Client) Get(url string) (resp *Response, err error)

### Client Registration Approaches

Source: https://modelcontextprotocol.io/specification/draft/basic/authorization

Overview of three client registration mechanisms supported by MCP: Client ID Metadata Documents, Pre-registration, and Dynamic Client Registration. Choose based on your scenario and relationship model.

```APIDOC
## Client Registration Approaches

### Overview
MCP supports three client registration mechanisms for different scenarios:

### 1. Client ID Metadata Documents

**Use Case:** When client and server have no prior relationship (most common)

**Description:**
Clients host their metadata at HTTPS URLs. Servers validate and cache documents.

**Implementation:**
- Client hosts metadata at `https://app.example.com/oauth/client-metadata.json`
- Client_id is the HTTPS URL to the metadata document
- Authorization server fetches and validates metadata
- Supports self-registration scenarios

**Advantages:**
- No pre-coordination required
- Suitable for dynamic client relationships
- Standards-based approach
- Supports decentralized architectures

**Requirements:**
- MCP clients **MUST** host metadata at HTTPS URL
- MCP clients **MUST** include client_id, client_name, redirect_uris
- Authorization servers **SHOULD** fetch and cache metadata
- Authorization servers **MUST** validate metadata structure and values

---

### 2. Pre-registration

**Use Case:** When client and server have an existing relationship

**Description:**
Clients and servers establish trust beforehand. Server has pre-configured client credentials.

**Implementation:**
- Server maintains client database with pre-registered client_ids
- No metadata discovery required
- Direct credential management
- Faster authorization flow

**Advantages:**
- Established trust relationship
- Reduced metadata overhead
- Better performance
- Full server control over client configuration

**Use Cases:**
- Enterprise integrations
- Known partner systems
- Internal organization tools
- Long-term integrations

---

### 3. Dynamic Client Registration

**Use Case:** For backwards compatibility or specific requirements

**Description:**
Clients register dynamically via registration endpoint at runtime.

**Implementation:**
- Client submits registration request to server
- Server issues client credentials
- Client uses credentials for subsequent requests
- Supports runtime client creation

**Advantages:**
- Runtime flexibility
- Programmatic registration
- Backwards compatible
- Supports emerging clients

**Use Cases:**
- Legacy system compatibility
- Ad-hoc client creation
- Development/testing scenarios
- Environments with dynamic client requirements

---

### Selection Criteria

| Scenario | Recommended Approach |
|----------|---------------------|
| Unknown clients, open ecosystem | Client ID Metadata Documents |
| Known partners, existing relationship | Pre-registration |
| Legacy systems, runtime flexibility | Dynamic Client Registration |
| Enterprise environment | Pre-registration |
| Public API, third-party integrations | Client ID Metadata Documents |
| Development/testing | Dynamic Client Registration |

### Implementation Notes

**For MCP Clients:**
- Choose registration approach based on server capabilities
- Implement metadata hosting for Client ID Metadata Documents
- Store pre-registered credentials securely
- Support dynamic registration if server requires it

**For MCP Servers:**
- Support at least Client ID Metadata Documents
- Implement appropriate validation for chosen mechanism
- Cache metadata to reduce latency
- Implement security policies for each approach
```

### GitHub Action for Vercel Preview Deployments (YAML)

Source: https://vercel.com/guides/how-can-i-use-github-actions-with-vercel

This GitHub Actions workflow automates the creation of Vercel Preview Deployments. It triggers on every push to branches other than 'main', checks out the code, installs the Vercel CLI, pulls environment information, builds the project artifacts, and deploys them to Vercel using the `--prebuilt` flag.

```yaml
name: Vercel Preview Deployment
env:
  VERCEL_ORG_ID: ${{ secrets.VERCEL_ORG_ID }}
  VERCEL_PROJECT_ID: ${{ secrets.VERCEL_PROJECT_ID }}
on:
  push:
    branches-ignore:
      - main
jobs:
  Deploy-Preview:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v2
      - name: Install Vercel CLI
        run: npm install --global vercel@latest
      - name: Pull Vercel Environment Information
        run: vercel pull --yes --environment=preview --token=${{ secrets.VERCEL_TOKEN }}
      - name: Build Project Artifacts
        run: vercel build --token=${{ secrets.VERCEL_TOKEN }}
      - name: Deploy Project Artifacts to Vercel
        run: vercel deploy --prebuilt --token=${{ secrets.VERCEL_TOKEN }}
```

### Vercel Route with Conditional Header Matching (vercel.json)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/configuration

This example demonstrates how to define a Vercel route that only rewrites requests to `/end` if the `X-Custom-Header` header's value starts with 'valid' and ends with 'value'. It utilizes the expressive `value` object with `pre` (prefix) and `suf` (suffix) properties for precise conditional matching.

```json
{
  "$schema": "https://openapi.vercel.sh/vercel.json",
  "routes": [
    {
      "src": "/start",
      "dest": "/end",
      "has": [
        {
          "type": "header",
          "key": "X-Custom-Header",
          "value": {
            "pre": "valid",
            "suf": "value"
          }
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

### Start Development Server with Child Process (TypeScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/vercel/blob/main/DEVELOPING_A_RUNTIME

An optional exported function for Vercel CLI's dev command. It spawns a child process to create an HTTP server for each request, returning the child's port and PID. IPC is used to get the ephemeral port from the child process.

```typescript
import { spawn } from 'child_process';
import { StartDevServerOptions } from '@vercel/build-utils';

export async function startDevServer(options: StartDevServerOptions) {
  // Create a child process which will create an HTTP server.
  //
  // Note: `my-runtime-dev-server` is an example dev server program name.
  // Your implementation will spawn a different program specific to your runtime.
  const child = spawn('my-runtime-dev-server', [options.entrypoint], {
    stdio: ['ignore', 'inherit', 'inherit', 'pipe'],
  });

  // In this example, the child process will write the port number to FD 3…
  const portPipe = child.stdio[3];
  const childPort = await new Promise(resolve => {
    portPipe.setEncoding('utf8');
    portPipe.once('data', data => {
      resolve(Number(data));
    });
  });

  return { pid: child.pid, port: childPort };
}
```

### Bun Installation Strategy: Isolated Installs

The `--linker isolated` option implements a pnpm-like installation strategy, creating strict dependency isolation. ### Force File Download with Content-Disposition Header in JavaScript

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/vercel-blob

Demonstrates how to force a file download in the browser by setting the 'content-disposition' header to 'attachment'. This is useful for preventing the browser from rendering certain file types directly. The example shows a typical setup for handling uploads with potential download forcing.

```javascript
import { put } from '@vercel/blob';

// Example of putting a blob with attachment disposition (conceptual)
// In a real scenario, this would be part of an upload handler.
async function uploadFile(file) {
  const filename = file.name;
  const blob = await put(filename, file, {
    access: 'public',
    // If content-disposition needs to be 'attachment', it's often handled
    // by Vercel Blob automatically based on MIME type or explicitly via options
    // if available in a specific SDK version or configuration.
    // Forcing attachment for all types is often the default or handled server-side.
  });
  return blob;
}
```

### Display Chat Messages and Tool Outputs in React

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/nextjs-app-router

Renders a list of chat messages, differentiating between user and AI roles. It also handles displaying structured data from tool calls, such as weather or temperature conversion results, by stringifying the tool's output.

```javascript
const { messages, sendMessage } = useChat();

return (
  // ... other JSX elements
  <div className="chat-messages">
    {messages.map((message, index) => (
      <div key={index} className={`message ${message.role}`}>
        {message.role === 'user' ? 'User: ' : 'AI: '}
        {message.parts.map((part, partIndex) => {
          switch (part.type) {
            case 'text':
              return <span key={partIndex}>{part.text}</span>;
            case 'tool-weather':
            case 'tool-convertFahrenheitToCelsius':
              return (
                <pre key={partIndex} className="tool-output">
                  {JSON.stringify(part.data, null, 2)}
                </pre>
              );
            default:
              return null;
          }
        })}
      </div>
    ))}
  </div>
  // ... input and send functionality
);
```

### prepareStep Callback for Custom Step Settings (JavaScript)

Source: https://ai-sdk.dev/docs/ai-sdk-core/tools-and-tool-calling

Demonstrates how to use the prepareStep callback to customize settings for individual steps, such as selecting a different model, forcing a tool choice, or limiting available tools. It also shows how to modify input messages for longer agentic loops, like prompt compression.

```javascript
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const result = await generateText({
  // ... other options
  prepareStep: async ({ model, stepNumber, steps, messages }) => {
    if (stepNumber === 0) {
      return {
        // use a different model for this step:
        model: modelForThisParticularStep,
        // force a tool choice for this step:
        toolChoice: {
          type: 'tool',
          toolName: 'tool1',
        },
        // limit the tools that are available for this step:
        activeTools: ['tool1'],
      };
    }
    // Compress conversation history for longer loops
    if (messages.length > 20) {
      return {
        messages: messages.slice(-10),
      };
    }
    // when nothing is returned, the default settings are used
    return {};
  },
});
```

### Example of Forbidden Fetch in Next.js Middleware

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/conformance/rules/NO_FETCH_FROM_MIDDLEWARE

This code demonstrates a scenario where a `fetch` call within a Next.js middleware, or its dependencies, would cause a build or runtime check to fail. The `experiments.ts` file uses `fetch` to get experiment data, and `middleware.ts` uses this function, leading to the disallowed asynchronous operation.

```typescript
export async function getExperiments() {
  const res = await fetch('/experiments');
  return res.json();
}
```

```typescript
export async function middleware( request: NextRequest,
  event: NextFetchEvent,
): Promise {
  const experiments = await getExperiments();
  if (experiments.includes('new-marketing-page)) {
    return NextResponse.rewrite(MARKETING_PAGE_URL);
  }
  return NextResponse.next();
}
```

### Configure Redis Server Storage with Nitro (TypeScript)

Source: https://nuxt.com/docs/guide/directory-structure/server

Set up Redis as a storage driver within Nitro configuration. This example shows how to define the Redis connection details in `nuxt.config.ts` and then use `useStorage('redis')` in API handlers to interact with the Redis instance for operations like getting, setting, or removing keys.

```typescript
import { defineNuxtConfig } from 'nuxt/config'

export default defineNuxtConfig({
  nitro: {
    storage: {
      redis: {
        driver: 'redis',
        /* redis connector options */
        port: 6379,
        host: '127.0.0.1',
        username: '',
        password: '',
        db: 0,
        tls: {},
      },
    },
  },
})
```

```typescript
import { defineEventHandler, useStorage } from 'h3'

export default defineEventHandler(async (event) => {
  // List all keys
  const keys = await useStorage('redis').getKeys()
  // Set a key
  await useStorage('redis').setItem('foo', 'bar')
  // Remove a key
  await useStorage('redis').removeItem('foo')
  return {}
})
```

### Define Getter on New Objects (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example demonstrates how to define a getter for a pseudo-property `latest` on a new object literal. The getter returns the last item of an array `log`. Assigning a value to `latest` will not change it, as it's controlled by the getter function.

```javascript
const obj = {
  log: [],
  get latest() {
    if (this.log.length === 0) {
      return undefined;
    }
    return this.log[this.log.length - 1];
  }
};

obj.log.push('first entry');
console.log(obj.latest); // 'first entry'
```

--------------------------------

### Stream Text with Multiple Tools - TypeScript/JavaScript

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/docs/getting-started/svelte

Creates an async POST handler that streams text responses from GPT-4o model with two tools: weather lookup and Fahrenheit to Celsius conversion. Uses Zod for schema validation and returns a UI message stream response.

```typescript
export async function POST({ request }) {
  const { messages }: { messages: UIMessage[] } = await request.json();
  const result = streamText({
    model: openai('gpt-4o'),
    messages: convertToModelMessages(messages),
    stopWhen: stepCountIs(5),
    tools: {
      weather: tool({
        description: 'Get the weather in a location (fahrenheit)',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          location: z.string().describe('The location to get the weather for'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ location }) => {
          const temperature = Math.round(Math.random() * (90 - 32) + 32);
          return { location, temperature };
        },
      }),
      convertFahrenheitToCelsius: tool({
        description: 'Convert a temperature in fahrenheit to celsius',
        inputSchema: z.object({
          temperature: z.number().describe('The temperature in fahrenheit to convert'),
        }),
        execute: async ({ temperature }) => {
          const celsius = Math.round((temperature - 32) * (5 / 9));
          return { celsius };
        },
      }),
    },
  });
  return result.toUIMessageStreamResponse();
}
```

### Send Binary Image Buffer in User Message (Node.js)

Shows how to include a binary image as a file buffer in a user message for analysis. This example uses Node.js's `fs.readFileSync` to get the image data and sends it using the `ai` SDK's `generateText` function. Requires the `fs` module.

const result = await generateText({
  model,

          type: 'text',
          text: 'Describe the image in detail.'

        {
          type: 'image',

### Matcher Configuration Examples (JavaScript)

Source: https://nextjs.org/docs/app/building-your-application/routing/middleware

Illustrates various ways to configure the `matcher` option in JavaScript for the proxy function. This includes matching single paths, multiple paths, using regular expressions to exclude specific routes, and a detailed example with `source`, `locale`, `has`, and `missing` properties.

```javascript
export const config = {
  matcher: ['/about/:path*', '/dashboard/:path*'], 
}
```

```javascript
export const config = {
  matcher: [
    // Exclude API routes, static files, image optimizations, and .png files
    '/((?!api|_next/static|_next/image|.*\.png$).*)',
  ],
}
```

```javascript
export const config = {
  matcher: [
    {
      source: '/api/:path*', 
      locale: false,
      has: [
        { type: 'header', key: 'Authorization', value: 'Bearer Token' },
        { type: 'query', key: 'userId', value: '123' },
      ],
      missing: [{ type: 'cookie', key: 'session', value: 'active' }],
    },
  ],
}
```

### Create Flags Discovery Endpoint in Next.js (route.ts)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/feature-flags/flags-explorer/getting-started

Creates the API endpoint for discovering feature flags in Next.js applications. This endpoint, typically located at `app/.well-known/vercel/flags/route.ts`, uses `createFlagsDiscoveryEndpoint` and `getProviderData` to automatically generate feature flag definitions based on your code. It ensures unauthorized requests are prevented using `verifyAccess`.

```typescript
import { getProviderData, createFlagsDiscoveryEndpoint } from 'flags/next';
import * as flags from '../../../../flags';

export const GET = createFlagsDiscoveryEndpoint(() => getProviderData(flags));
```

### Add Global and Named Middleware Dynamically in Nuxt Plugin

```typescript
export default defineNuxtPlugin(() => {

    console.log('this global middleware was added in a plugin and will be run on every route change')
  }, { global: true })

### Fortran 2003 Example for Standard Input/Output

Source: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_streams

Shows how to read an integer from the standard input unit (INPUT_UNIT) and write it to the standard output unit (OUTPUT_UNIT) using Fortran 2003's ISO_FORTRAN_ENV module for portability.

```fortran
! Fortran 2003 example
program main
use iso_fortran_env
implicit none
integer :: number
read (unit=INPUT_UNIT,*) number
write (unit=OUTPUT_UNIT,'(a,i3)') 'Number is: ', number
end program
```

### Install and Use Semver as a Node.js Module

Source: https://docs.npmjs.com/cli/v6/using-npm/semver

Installs the semver package using npm and demonstrates its usage within a Node.js application for validating, cleaning, satisfying, comparing, and coercing semantic versions.

```bash
npm install --save semver
```

```javascript
const semver = require("semver");
semver.valid("1.2.3"); // '1.2.3'
semver.valid("a.b.c"); // null
semver.clean(" =v1.2.3 "); // '1.2.3'
semver.satisfies("1.2.3", "1.x || >=2.5.0 || 5.0.0 - 7.2.3"); // true
semver.gt("1.2.3", "9.8.7"); // false
semver.lt("1.2.3", "9.8.7"); // true
semver.minVersion(">=1.0.0"); // '1.0.0'
semver.valid(semver.coerce("v2")); // '2.0.0'
semver.valid(semver.coerce("42.6.7.9.3-alpha")); // '42.6.7'
```

--------------------------------

### Use Getters in Classes (JavaScript)

Source: https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Functions/get

This example shows how to define a public instance getter within a JavaScript class. The getter `fullName` is defined on the class prototype and is shared across all instances. Unlike object literals, getter properties in classes are not enumerable by default.

```javascript
class Person {
  constructor(firstName, lastName) {
    this.firstName = firstName;
    this.lastName = lastName;
  }

  get fullName() {
    return `${this.firstName} ${this.lastName}`;
  }
}

const person = new Person('John', 'Doe');
console.log(person.fullName); // 'John Doe'
```

### Export Environment Variable in npm Script (Incorrect Pattern)

Source: https://turborepo.com/docs/crafting-your-repository/using-environment-variables

Example showing an incorrect pattern where environment variables are exported inline during task execution. This approach fails because Turborepo hashes environment variables at task start, before the export occurs, so the variable won't be included in task hashing or cache invalidation.

    "dev": "export MY_VARIABLE=123 && next dev"

### Encrypting Parameters for Image Generation

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Learn how to encrypt sensitive parameters used in image generation URLs, ensuring that only specific values can be passed and preventing unauthorized access or manipulation. This method enhances security for dynamic image generation. The example outlines the concept, typically involving server-side encryption/decryption.

```plaintext
# Concept:
# 1. Client requests an image with a token.
# 2. Server encrypts the sensitive parameters (e.g., user ID, data) with a secret key.
# 3. Server generates a URL with the encrypted token.
# 4. Client shares the URL.
# 5. When the image generation endpoint is hit:
#    a. The server receives the encrypted token.
#    b. The server decrypts the token using the secret key.
#    c. The server uses the decrypted parameters to generate the image.
#    d. If decryption fails or parameters are invalid, an error or default image is returned.
```

### HTTP Server Management

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Functions for starting and managing HTTP servers, including handling TLS connections and default multiplexer registration.

```APIDOC
## func ListenAndServe

### Description
Listens on the TCP network address `addr` and then calls `Serve` with `handler` to handle requests on incoming connections. Accepted connections are configured to enable TCP keep-alives. The handler is typically nil, in which case `DefaultServeMux` is used. `ListenAndServe` always returns a non-nil error.

### Method
`ListenAndServe`

### Endpoint
N/A (Server function)

### Parameters
* **addr** (string) - Required - The network address to listen on (e.g., ":8080").
* **handler** (Handler) - Optional - The handler to use for requests. If nil, `DefaultServeMux` is used.

### Response
#### Success Response (0)
Returns nil if the server starts successfully. Errors are returned if the server fails to start.

#### Response Example
`nil` (on success)

```

```APIDOC
## func ListenAndServeTLS

### Description
Acts identically to `ListenAndServe`, except that it expects HTTPS connections. Additionally, files containing a certificate and matching private key for the server must be provided. If the certificate is signed by a certificate authority, the `certFile` should be the concatenation of the server's certificate, any intermediates, and the CA's certificate.

### Method
`ListenAndServeTLS`

### Endpoint
N/A (Server function)

### Parameters
* **addr** (string) - Required - The network address to listen on (e.g., ":8443").
* **certFile** (string) - Required - Path to the TLS certificate file.
* **keyFile** (string) - Required - Path to the TLS private key file.
* **handler** (Handler) - Optional - The handler to use for requests. If nil, `DefaultServeMux` is used.

### Response
#### Success Response (0)
Returns nil if the server starts successfully. Errors are returned if the server fails to start or if certificate/key files are invalid.

#### Response Example
`nil` (on success)

```

```APIDOC
## func Handle

### Description
Registers the handler for the given pattern in `DefaultServeMux`. The documentation for `ServeMux` explains how patterns are matched.

### Method
`Handle`

### Endpoint
N/A (Registration function)

### Parameters
* **pattern** (string) - Required - The URL pattern to match (e.g., "/static/").
* **handler** (Handler) - Required - The handler to register for the pattern.

### Response
This function does not return a value.

```

```APIDOC
## func HandleFunc

### Description
Registers the handler function for the given pattern in `DefaultServeMux`. The documentation for `ServeMux` explains how patterns are matched.

### Method
`HandleFunc`

### Endpoint
N/A (Registration function)

### Parameters
* **pattern** (string) - Required - The URL pattern to match (e.g., "/hello").
* **handler** (func(ResponseWriter, *Request)) - Required - The handler function to register.

### Response
This function does not return a value.

```

### Stream Responses from LLMs (Vercel)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Explore how to implement streaming responses from Large Language Models (LLMs) on Vercel. This provides a more interactive user experience by sending back data as it's generated, rather than waiting for the entire response. The example uses server-sent events (SSE) or chunked transfer encoding.

```typescript
import type { VercelRequest, VercelResponse } from '@vercel/node';

export default async (req: VercelRequest, res: VercelResponse) => {
  // Set headers for Server-Sent Events (SSE)
  res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'text/event-stream');
  res.setHeader('Cache-Control', 'no-cache');
  res.setHeader('Connection', 'keep-alive');

  // Simulate LLM response streaming
  const streamData = async () => {
    const chunks = ['This ', 'is ', 'a ', 'streaming ', 'response ', 'from ', 'an ', 'LLM.'];
    for (const chunk of chunks) {
      res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify({ text: chunk })}\n\n`);
      await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 200)); // Simulate delay
    }
    res.end(); // Signal end of stream
  };

  await streamData();
};
```

### Handling Backpressure in Streams (Node.js)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Learn how to effectively manage backpressure in Node.js streams, ensuring that data is pushed into a stream only when it's ready to be processed. This prevents memory issues and improves application stability when dealing with large amounts of data or slow consumers. The example uses readable and writable streams.

```javascript
const fs = require('fs');
const readline = require('readline');

const readableStream = fs.createReadStream('large_file.txt');
const writableStream = fs.createWriteStream('output.txt');

const rl = readline.createInterface({
  input: readableStream,
  crlfDelay: Infinity // Recognize all instances of CR LF ('\r\n') as a single line break.
});

rl.on('line', (line) => {
  // Simulate a slow processing step
  setTimeout(() => {
    writableStream.write(line + '\n', () => {
      // Callback ensures the write is complete before the next line is processed
      // This implicitly handles backpressure because writableStream.write will pause
      // the readable stream if its buffer is full.
    });
  }, 100); // Simulate 100ms processing time
});

rl.on('close', () => {
  writableStream.end();
  console.log('Processing complete.');
});

// Handle potential errors
readableStream.on('error', (err) => console.error('Readable stream error:', err));
writableStream.on('error', (err) => console.error('Writable stream error:', err));
```

### GET /

Source: https://docs.astro.build/en/reference/api-reference

A basic GET endpoint that demonstrates accessing request URL information. Note that search parameters may not be present on prerendered pages.

```APIDOC

### Serve Files from a FileSystem in Go

Source: https://golang.org/pkg/net/http

Details functions for serving files from a given `FileSystem`. `FileServer` creates a handler that serves files from a `http.FileSystem`, while `FileServerFS` does the same but uses an `fs.FS` interface, making it compatible with the newer `io/fs` package.

```go
// Creates a handler that serves HTTP requests with the content of the file system rooted at root.
// To use the package, create a http.FileSystem using fileSystem, for example:
// var fs http.FileSystem = http.Dir(".")
// http.Handle("/static/", http.FileServer(fs))
func FileServer(root FileSystem) Handler

// FileServerFS returns a handler that serves HTTP requests with the contents of the
// file system rooted at root. 
func FileServerFS(root fs.FS) Handler
```

### Configure Forbidden Code Rule in Vercel Conformance

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/conformance/custom-rules/forbidden-code

Creates a custom forbidden-code rule configuration that disallows specific strings and patterns. This example demonstrates how to disallow usage of 'and' at line start, 'but' in any case, and 'TODO' comments. Configure this in your conformance.config.jsonc file with required properties like ruleType, ruleName, errorMessage, patterns, and strings.

```json
{
  "customRules": [
    {
      "ruleType": "forbidden-code",
      "ruleName": "NO_DISALLOWED_USAGE",
      "categories": ["code-health"],
      "errorMessage": "Usage of this code pattern is not allowed",
      "errorLink": "https://example.com/docs",
      "description": "Disallows specific strings and patterns in codebase",
      "severity": "major",
      "patterns": [
        "^and",
        {
          "pattern": "but",
          "flags": "i"
        }
      ],
      "strings": ["TODO"]
    }
  ]
}
```

### Nuxt Runtime Configuration Example

Source: https://nuxt.com/docs/api/configuration/nuxt-config

Demonstrates setting up runtime configuration in Nuxt. This allows passing dynamic configuration and environment variables to the Nuxt app context. 'apiKey' is private and server-only, while 'baseURL' under 'public' is exposed to the frontend.

```javascript
export default defineNuxtConfig({
  runtimeConfig: {
    apiKey: '', // Default to an empty string, automatically set at runtime using process.env.NUXT_API_KEY
    public: {
      baseURL: '', // Exposed to the frontend as well.
    },
  },
})
```

### Build a Weather API with FastAPI and Vercel

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/integrating-next-js-and-contentful-for-your-headless-cms

This guide shows how to create a simple FastAPI backend to provide real-time weather data. It includes a single route for accessing weather information.

```python
from fastapi import FastAPI
import requests

app = FastAPI()

@app.get('/weather')
def get_weather(location: str):
    api_key = "YOUR_WEATHER_API_KEY"
    base_url = "http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?"
    complete_url = base_url + "appid=" + api_key + "&q=" + location
    response = requests.get(complete_url)
    data = response.json()

    if data["cod"] != "404":
        main = data["main"]
        temperature = main["temp"]
        return {"location": location, "temperature": temperature}
    else:
        return {"error": "City not found"}
```

### POST /deployments - Force Build Execution

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/builds/managing-builds

Trigger immediate build execution for a queued deployment using the Start Building Now action. This endpoint allows you to bypass the queue and proceed with building regardless of the queuing reason.

```APIDOC
## POST /deployments/{deploymentId}/start-build

### Description
Force an on-demand build for a specific deployment that is currently queued. This endpoint processes the deployment immediately, bypassing the build queue regardless of the reason for queueing.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
https://api.vercel.com/v9/deployments/{deploymentId}/start-build

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **deploymentId** (string) - Required - The unique identifier of the deployment to build

#### Query Parameters
- **teamId** (string) - Optional - The team ID associated with the deployment

### Request Example
```json
{}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **deploymentId** (string) - The deployment identifier
- **status** (string) - Current deployment status (building)
- **buildStartedAt** (timestamp) - When the build was initiated

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "deploymentId": "dpl_xxxxx",
  "status": "building",
  "buildStartedAt": 1702468800000
}
```

### Manual Dashboard Steps
1. Select your project from the Vercel dashboard
2. Navigate to the Deployments tab from the top navigation
3. Use the Status filter to locate your queued deployment
4. Either:
   - Click the three dots menu on the deployment and select "Start Building Now"
   - Click the deployment to open its detail page and click "Start Building Now"
5. Confirm the action in the dialog that appears

### Notes
- Available on all Vercel plans
- Only applicable to deployments with status "queued"
- Immediately removes deployment from the build queue
```

### Generate GitHub App Installation Access Token using cURL

Source: https://docs.github.com/en/apps/creating-github-apps/authenticating-with-a-github-app/generating-an-installation-access-token-for-a-github-app

This snippet demonstrates how to send a POST request to the GitHub API to generate an installation access token. It requires a JSON web token (JWT) for authentication and allows optional scoping of repositories and permissions. The generated token has a 1-hour lifespan.

```curl
--request POST \
--url "https://api.github.com/app/installations/INSTALLATION_ID/access_tokens" \
--header "Accept: application/vnd.github+json" \
--header "Authorization: Bearer JWT" \
--header "X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28"
```

s := &http.Server{
    Addr:           ":8080",

    ReadTimeout:    10 * time.Second,
    WriteTimeout:   10 * time.Second,
    MaxHeaderBytes: 1 << 20,
}

### Create a Simple Counter with TanStack Store

Source: https://vercel.com/templates/starter/tanstack-start-on-vercel

Implements a basic counter using TanStack Store. It demonstrates creating a store, accessing its state, and updating it using `setState`.

```typescript
import { useStore } from "@tanstack/react-store";
import { Store } from "@tanstack/store";
import "./App.css";

const countStore = new Store(0);

function App() {
  const count = useStore(countStore);
  return (
    <div>
      <button onClick={() => countStore.setState((n) => n + 1)}>
        Increment - {count}
      </button>
    </div>
  );
}

export default App;
```

### Initialize Sentry with Custom OpenTelemetry Setup - Node.js

Source: https://docs.sentry.io/platforms/javascript/guides/nextjs/opentelemetry/custom-setup

Configures Sentry with a custom OpenTelemetry NodeTracerProvider by setting skipOpenTelemetrySetup to true and manually adding SentrySpanProcessor, SentryPropagator, SentrySampler, and SentryContextManager. This setup ensures proper trace sampling, propagation, context management, and span processing for both error monitoring and distributed tracing.

```javascript
const Sentry = require("@sentry/node");
const { SentrySpanProcessor, SentryPropagator, SentrySampler } = require("@sentry/opentelemetry");
const { NodeTracerProvider } = require("@opentelemetry/sdk-trace-node");

const sentryClient = Sentry.init({
  dsn: "https://examplePublicKey@o0.ingest.sentry.io/0",
  skipOpenTelemetrySetup: true,
  tracesSampleRate: 1.0
});

const provider = new NodeTracerProvider({
  sampler: sentryClient ? new SentrySampler(sentryClient) : undefined,
  spanProcessors: [
    new SentrySpanProcessor()
  ]
});

provider.register({
  propagator: new SentryPropagator(),
  contextManager: new Sentry.SentryContextManager()
});

Sentry.validateOpenTelemetrySetup();
```

### Block Traffic in Specific Countries with Vercel WAF API

```json

  "version": "7.4",
  "rule": {
    "id": "BLOCK_SPECIFIC_COUNTRIES",
    "action": {"type": "BLOCK"},
    "matches": [
      {"type": "COUNTRY", "country": ["CN", "RU", "KP"]}

### Dynamically Generate OG Image with URL Parameters (Next.js)

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/guides/how-to-allowlist-deployment-ip-address

Learn how to create Open Graph (OG) images dynamically by passing text content, such as an image title, as a URL parameter. This enables personalized or up-to-date OG images for your shared links. The example uses a combination of serverless functions and image manipulation libraries.

```typescript
import { ImageResponse } from '@vercel/og'
import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'

export async function GET(request: NextRequest) {
  const { searchParams } = new URL(request.url)
  const title = searchParams.get('title') || 'Default Title'

  return new ImageResponse(
    (
      <div
        style={{
          fontSize: 72,
          background: 'white',
          width: '100%',
          height: '100%',
          display: 'flex',
          alignItems: 'center',
          justifyContent: 'center',
        }}
      >
        {title}
      </div>
    ),
    { width: 1200, height: 630 }
  )
}
```

### Initialize Satori Standalone Build with WASM (JavaScript)

Source: https://github.com/vercel/satori

This example shows how to initialize the Satori standalone build by manually loading the `yoga.wasm` binary. It uses the `fetch` API to retrieve the WASM file from a CDN and then passes the ArrayBuffer to the `init` function. After initialization, Satori can be used as usual.

```javascript
import satori, { init } from 'satori/standalone'
const res = await fetch('https://unpkg.com/satori/yoga.wasm')
const yogaWasm = await res.arrayBuffer()
await init(yogaWasm)
// Now you can use satori as usual
const svg = await satori(...)
```

### PUT /v1/installations - Upsert Installation

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/create-integration/marketplace-api

Upsert an installation record for a Vercel marketplace integration. This endpoint creates a new installation or updates an existing one with the provided configuration and credentials.

```APIDOC
## PUT /v1/installations

### Description
Upsert (create or update) an installation record for a Vercel marketplace integration. This endpoint manages the installation configuration and credentials for integrations.

### Method
PUT

### Endpoint
/v1/installations

### Authentication
- Bearer Token
- System Authentication (OIDC)

### Request Body
- **credentials** (string) - Required - The access token/credentials for the integration
- **configuration** (object) - Required - Installation configuration object
- **installation_id** (string) - Optional - The ID of the installation to update

### Request Example
PUT /v1/installations
Authorization: Bearer access_token_here
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "credentials": "provider_access_token",
  "configuration": {
    "enabled": true,
    "settings": {}
  }
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200/201)
- **installation_id** (string) - The ID of the installation
- **status** (string) - Status of the installation (e.g., "active")
- **created_at** (string) - Installation creation timestamp
- **updated_at** (string) - Last update timestamp

#### Response Example
{
  "installation_id": "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p",
  "status": "active",
  "created_at": "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z",
  "updated_at": "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z"
}
```

### Extract structured data using Python SDK

Source: https://platform.openai.com/docs/guides/structured-outputs

This Python code snippet demonstrates how to extract structured event information from unstructured text using the OpenAI SDK and Pydantic for schema definition. It defines a `CalendarEvent` model and uses the `client.responses.parse` method to get a parsed output conforming to the schema. Ensure the `openai` and `pydantic` libraries are installed.

```python
from openai import OpenAI
from pydantic import BaseModel

client = OpenAI()

class CalendarEvent(BaseModel):
    name: str
    date: str
    participants: list[str]

response = client.responses.parse(
    model="gpt-4o-2024-08-06",
    input=[
        {"role": "system", "content": "Extract the event information."},
        { "role": "user", "content": "Alice and Bob are going to a science fair on Friday.", },
    ],
    text_format=CalendarEvent,
)

event = response.output_parsed
```

### Absolute Path Handling with CWD on Windows

Source: https://github.com/isaacs/node-glob

Explains the behavior when a pattern starts with '/' and an explicit 'cwd' option is provided on Windows, especially when the 'cwd' includes a drive letter. The example shows that the drive letter from the 'cwd' is used as the root for directory traversal, as seen in `glob('/tmp', { cwd: 'c:/any/thing' })` returning `['c:/tmp']`.

```javascript
// Example: Traversal rooted at c: drive when cwd is specified
// glob('/tmp', { cwd: 'c:/any/thing' }); // Returns ['c:/tmp']
```

### Next.js Server Component Example

Source: https://nextjs.org/docs/app/building-your-application/rendering/server-components

An example of a Next.js Server Component that fetches post data and renders it. It imports a Client Component (LikeButton) and uses async/await for data fetching. This component runs exclusively on the server.

```TypeScript
import LikeButton from '@/app/ui/like-button'
import { getPost } from '@/lib/data'

export default async function Page({ params, }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }) {
  const { id } = await params
  const post = await getPost(id)
  return (
    <>
      <h1>{post.title}</h1>
      <p>============</p>
      {/* ... */}
      <LikeButton likes={post.likes} />
    </>
  )
}
```

### PATCH /v1/installations/{installationId}

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/integrations/marketplace-api

Update an existing installation with new billing plan and notification settings. Requires User Authentication for secure modification.

```APIDOC
## PATCH /v1/installations/{installationId}

### Description
Update an installation. Modify the billing plan and notification settings for an existing installation.

### Method
PATCH

### Endpoint
`/v1/installations/{installationId}`

### Security
User Authentication required

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **installationId** (string) - Required - The ID of the installation. Example: "icfg_9bceb8ccT32d3U417ezb5c8p"

#### Request Body
- **billingPlan** (object) - Optional - The billing plan for the installation
- **notification** (object or null) - Optional - Installation's active notification

### Request Example
{
  "billingPlan": {
    "planName": "enterprise"
  },
  "notification": null
}

### Response
#### Success Response (200/204)
- **billingPlan** (object) - The updated billing plan for the installation
- **notification** (object or null) - The updated installation notification

#### Error Responses
- **400** - Bad Request
- **403** - Forbidden
- **409** - Conflict
```

### Enable Live Search with xAI Grok

Source: https://sdk.vercel.ai/providers/ai-sdk-providers/xai

Example of enabling and configuring Live Search for xAI Grok models to include real-time data and citations in responses.

```typescript
import { xai } from '@ai-sdk/xai';
import { generateText } from 'ai';

const { text, sources } = await generateText({
  model: xai('grok-3-latest'),
  prompt: 'What are the latest developments in AI?',
  providerOptions: {
    xai: {
      searchParameters: {
        mode: 'auto', // 'auto', 'on', or 'off'
        returnCitations: true,
        maxSearchResults: 5,
      },
    },
  },
});

console.log(text);
console.log('Sources:', sources);
```

### GET http.get()

Source: https://nodejs.org/api/http.html

Convenience method for making GET requests. Automatically sets the HTTP method to GET and calls req.end(). Accepts URL and options parameters with an optional callback for handling the response.

```APIDOC
## GET http.get()

### Description
Convenience method for making HTTP GET requests. Sets method to GET by default and automatically calls req.end(). Most requests are GET requests without bodies, making this utility method more efficient than http.request().

### Method
GET

### Signatures
- http.get(options[, callback])
- http.get(url[, options][, callback])

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **url** (string | URL) - Optional - Request URL. Can be a WHATWG URL object (v7.5.0+)
- **options** (object) - Optional - Same options as http.request() with method defaulting to GET
- **callback** (function) - Optional - Invoked with single argument (http.IncomingMessage)

### Request Example
```javascript
http.get('http://localhost:8000/', (res) => {
  const { statusCode } = res;
  const contentType = res.headers['content-type'];
  let error;
  
  if (statusCode !== 200) {
    error = new Error(`Request Failed. Status Code: ${statusCode}`);
  }
  
  if (error) {
    console.error(error.message);
    res.resume();
    return;
  }
  
  res.setEncoding('utf8');
  let rawData = '';
  
  res.on('data', (chunk) => {
    rawData += chunk;
  });
  
  res.on('end', () => {
    try {
      const parsedData = JSON.parse(rawData);
      console.log(parsedData);
    } catch (e) {
      console.error(e.message);
    }
  });
});
```

### Response
#### Success Response (2xx Status Code)
- **statusCode** (number) - HTTP response status code
- **headers** (object) - Response headers including content-type
- **data** (string/buffer) - Response body data

#### Error Handling
- Callback must consume response data to free up memory
- Check statusCode for non-2xx responses
- Use res.resume() to drain socket on errors
```

export default [
  js.configs.recommended,
  importPlugin.flatConfigs.recommended,
  {
    files: ['**/*.{js,mjs,cjs}'],
    languageOptions: {
      ecmaVersion: 'latest',
      sourceType: 'module'
    },
    rules: {
      'no-unused-vars': 'off',
      'import/no-dynamic-require': 'warn',
      'import/no-nodejs-modules': 'warn'
    }
  }
];
```

### Locate Good Region in Damaged Repository Object Graph

Source: https://git-scm.com/docs/git-bisect

This example demonstrates how to locate a good region within a damaged repository's object graph using git bisect. It starts a bisect session without checking out the working tree, then uses 'git for-each-ref' and 'git rev-list' to identify good commits and temporary files for processing.

```shell
$ git bisect start HEAD \
    [...] \
    --no-checkout
$ git bisect run sh -c ' GOOD=$(git for-each-ref "--format=%(objectname)" refs/bisect/good-*) && git rev-list --objects BISECT_HEAD --not $GOOD >tmp.$$ && git pack-objects --stdout >/dev/null'
```

### Express Middleware Sub-stack Example (JavaScript)

app.use('/user/:id', (req, res, next) => {
  console.log('Request URL:', req.originalUrl)
  next()
}, (req, res, next) => {
  console.log('Request Type:', req.method)
  next()
})
```

### Node.js Pagination Example for Vercel Projects

Source: https://vercel.com/docs/rest-api/reference/welcome

This Node.js script demonstrates how to fetch all projects from the Vercel API, handling pagination using the `until` query parameter and saving the results to a JSON file. It uses the `axios` library for making HTTP requests and `fs` for file system operations. Ensure you replace 'yourtokenvalue' with your actual Vercel API token.

```javascript
const axios = require('axios');
const fs = require('fs');
const vercelToken = 'yourtokenvalue'; //Replace with your token
const apiEndPt = 'https://api.vercel.com/v9/projects';
let config = {
  method: 'get',
  url: apiEndPt,
  headers: {
    Authorization: 'Bearer ' + vercelToken,
  },
};
let results = [];
(function loop() {
  axios(config)
    .then(function (response) {
      results.push(...response.data.projects);
      if (response.data.pagination.next !== null) {
        config.url = `${apiEndPt}?until=${response.data.pagination.next}`;
        loop();
      } else {
        //you can use the final results object and for example save it to a json file
        fs.writeFileSync('projects.json', JSON.stringify(results));
      }
    })
    .catch(function (error) {
      console.log(error);
    });
})();
```

### Next.js Client Component Example (Counter)

Source: https://nextjs.org/docs/app/building-your-application/rendering/server-components

An example of a Next.js Client Component demonstrating state management with `useState`. The 'use client' directive is crucial here, making the entire component and its children part of the client bundle.

```TypeScript
'use client'
import { useState } from 'react'

export default function Counter() {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0)
  return (
    <>
      <p>{count} likes</p>
      <button onClick={() => setCount(count + 1)}>Click me</button>
    </>
  )
}
```

--------------------------------

### Configure FNM for Windows Command Prompt (Batch)

Source: https://github.com/Schniz/fnm

Sets up FNM initialization script for cmd.exe with guard to prevent infinite loops. Add this startup script to cmd.exe or Windows Terminal to enable FNM's automatic Node.js version management in Command Prompt.

```batch
@echo off
:: for /F will launch a new instance of cmd so we create a guard to prevent an infnite loop
if not defined FNM_AUTORUN_GUARD (
  set "FNM_AUTORUN_GUARD=AutorunGuard"
  FOR /f "tokens=*" %%z IN ('fnm env --use-on-cd') DO CALL %%z
)
```
